# Token Savior Go Port — M2 Implementation Plan

> **For agentic workers:** REQUIRED SUB-SKILL: Use superpowers:subagent-driven-development (recommended) or superpowers:executing-plans to implement this plan task-by-task. Steps use checkbox (`- [ ]`) syntax for tracking.

**Goal:** Extend the Go `token-savior` binary with four new language annotators (shell, TypeScript, Rust, Java) and seven new navigation tools (`get_function_source`, `get_class_source`, `get_dependents`, `get_dependencies`, `get_change_impact`, `get_full_context`, `get_call_chain`). Land per-language fidelity tooling so the E5 gate (≥95% recall, ≥98% precision per language vs Python) is measurable in CI. Land cold-index timing so the E2 gate (Go ≤ Python +10%) is measurable. Compat harness stays green for the combined M1+M2 tool set.

**Architecture:** Four new annotator sub-packages register themselves via `init() → annotator.Register(lang, New())`, mirroring the M1 `internal/annotator/golang` shape. All four are **hand-rolled tokenizers** — no tree-sitter, no WASM, no external grammar (spec §169). Seven new query functions in `internal/query/` operate on the same `models.ProjectIndex` populated by `internal/indexer`; `get_dependents` and `get_dependencies` reverse-walk and forward-walk the existing `DepGraph` map; `get_change_impact` and `get_call_chain` are BFS over that graph; `get_full_context` is a composite. New MCP handlers in `internal/mcp/handlers.go` follow the existing SLOT-shape pattern. Tool schemas extended in `internal/tools/schemas.go` (M1's `m1Schemas` slice gets an `m2Schemas` sibling). `internal/compat/expected_diffs.go` extended for each new tool that diverges from Python's wire shape. New scripts/fidelity.sh runs Python vs Go side-by-side per language and emits the E5 JSON report.

**Tech Stack:** Go 1.26, no new external module deps beyond M1's `github.com/mark3labs/mcp-go` + `github.com/stretchr/testify`. All four annotators are pure-stdlib (`bufio`, `bytes`, `strings`, `unicode/utf8`). Fidelity script is bash + `jq` (already a dev requirement).

**Exit gate:** E1 (M1+M2 tool parity on per-language Small fixtures) + E2 (Go cold-index ≤ Python +10% on go-small / ts-small / java-small / rust-small / shell-small) + E5 (≥95% recall, ≥98% precision per language on the same fixtures, measured by `scripts/fidelity.sh`).

---

## Phase 1: Shell annotator (proves the non-Go annotator path)

Shell is greenfield (spec §175 — no Python equivalent). It's the smallest of the four new annotators, so it's the right place to prove the hand-rolled-tokenizer pattern before the larger TypeScript work. Scope is narrow on purpose: function definitions, aliases, source/dot imports, no call edges.

## Task 1: Shell annotator skeleton + dispatch registration

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/shell/annotator.go`, `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/empty.sh.txt`, `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/comments_only.sh.txt`

This task lands the package skeleton: `New()`, `Annotate()` returning a zero-result `StructuralMetadata` for an empty file, and the `init()` registration. The actual feature work (function detection, aliases, source) is tasks 2–3. By landing the registration first we can be sure the indexer-side wiring isn't subtly broken before we layer tokenizer logic on top.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create fixture files**

Create `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/empty.sh.txt` with empty content (zero bytes).

Create `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/comments_only.sh.txt`:
```
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# This file is just comments.
# Nothing else.
```

Fixtures use the `.sh.txt` suffix (NOT `.sh`) to keep `go test` and `goimports` from treating them as real shell sources — the Go build system tolerates `*.txt` happily and the `_test.go` file reads them with `os.ReadFile`. This pattern is carried forward from M1's `.go.txt` convention (see M1 status doc §"What landed at T22-T23").

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing skeleton test**

Create `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`:
```go
package shell

import (
	"os"
	"path/filepath"
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"

	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
)

func TestNew_Registers(t *testing.T) {
	require.NotNil(t, annotator.AnnotatorFor("foo.sh"), "shell annotator should be registered for .sh")
	require.NotNil(t, annotator.AnnotatorFor("foo.bash"), "shell annotator should be registered for .bash")
	require.NotNil(t, annotator.AnnotatorFor("foo.zsh"), "shell annotator should be registered for .zsh")
}

func TestAnnotate_EmptyFile(t *testing.T) {
	a := New()
	md, err := a.Annotate("empty.sh", nil)
	require.NoError(t, err)
	require.NotNil(t, md)
	require.Equal(t, "shell", md.Language)
	require.Equal(t, "empty.sh", md.Path)
	require.Empty(t, md.Functions)
	require.Empty(t, md.Classes)
	require.Empty(t, md.Imports)
}

func TestAnnotate_CommentsOnly(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "comments_only.sh.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("comments_only.sh", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)
	require.Empty(t, md.Functions)
	require.Empty(t, md.Imports)
}

// mustReadFixture loads testdata/<name> as bytes.
func mustReadFixture(t *testing.T, name string) []byte {
	t.Helper()
	raw, err := os.ReadFile(filepath.Join("testdata", name))
	require.NoError(t, err)
	return raw
}
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Run the test to verify it fails**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/shell/ -v
```
Expected: FAIL with `no Go files in internal/annotator/shell` — the package doesn't exist yet.

- [ ] **Step 4: Create the skeleton `internal/annotator/shell/annotator.go`**

```go
// Package shell annotates POSIX-ish shell source (.sh/.bash/.zsh).
//
// This is a hand-rolled, regex-light tokenizer — no tree-sitter, no external
// grammars. Scope: function definitions ("name() {…}" and "function name {…}"),
// alias declarations, and source/dot imports. Call edges are intentionally
// dropped (every command invocation looks like a call in shell — the
// signal-to-noise ratio is unworkable; see comments in Task 4).
package shell

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

func init() {
	annotator.Register("shell", New())
}

// Annotator is the shell-language annotator. Safe for concurrent use.
type Annotator struct{}

// New returns a shell annotator.
func New() *Annotator { return &Annotator{} }

// Annotate parses shell source and emits structural metadata.
//
// Parse errors are extremely rare — the recogniser is line-oriented and a
// malformed line is silently skipped, matching the lenient posture of the
// other M2 annotators. We never return an error from this path; the indexer
// would log it per-file and continue, but there's nothing to log.
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "shell",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	return md, nil
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests to verify they pass**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/shell/ -v
```
Expected: PASS for all three tests.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/shell/
git commit -m "feat(annotator/shell): skeleton + dispatch registration

Greenfield annotator (no Python equivalent — spec §175). This commit
lands the package, the init()-time registration for .sh/.bash/.zsh, and
a zero-result Annotate() so the indexer can dispatch into us. Function /
alias / source parsing land in T2-T3."
```

## Task 2: Function definition tokenizer

**Files:**
- Modify: `internal/annotator/shell/annotator.go`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/functions.sh.txt`

Shell function definitions take two forms (POSIX + bash extension):

```
foo() { … }            # POSIX: name() { body }
function bar { … }     # bash:  function name { body }
function baz() { … }   # bash:  function name() { body } (both keywords)
```

The recogniser walks lines; when it sees a function header it records line/end-line by counting braces from the opening `{` to the matching `}`. Heredocs (`<<EOF` / `<<-EOF`) suspend brace counting until the heredoc closer. Single-quoted strings are taken literally; double-quoted strings honour `\"` and `\$` escapes.

Edge cases the M2 plan accepts as lossy (don't fix in this pass):
- Functions defined inside other functions (rare; the outer function's end-line is still correct).
- Brace inside a `[[ … ]]` test expression that doesn't actually open a block (parser-level disambiguation would require a real shell tokenizer).
- Anonymous one-liners like `f() echo hi` (no braces) — recorded with EndLine == Line.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/functions.sh.txt`:
```
#!/usr/bin/env bash

# POSIX-style
deploy() {
    echo "deploying $1"
    helper "$1"
}

# bash-style with the `function` keyword, no parens
function rollback {
    echo "rolling back"
}

# bash-style with both keyword and parens
function status() {
    echo "status check"
}

# One-liner without braces — rare but legal.
ping_check() echo ping

# Nested braces inside the body
build() {
    if [[ "$1" == "release" ]]; then
        echo "release build"
    fi
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Append to `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestAnnotate_FunctionsPOSIXStyle(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.sh.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("functions.sh", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	byName := indexByName(md.Functions)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "deploy")
	require.Equal(t, 4, byName["deploy"].Line)
	require.Equal(t, 7, byName["deploy"].EndLine)
}

func TestAnnotate_FunctionsKeywordStyle(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.sh.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("functions.sh", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	byName := indexByName(md.Functions)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "rollback")
	require.Equal(t, 10, byName["rollback"].Line)
	require.Equal(t, 12, byName["rollback"].EndLine)

	require.Contains(t, byName, "status")
	require.Equal(t, 15, byName["status"].Line)
}

func TestAnnotate_FunctionWithNestedBraces(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.sh.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("functions.sh", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	byName := indexByName(md.Functions)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "build")
	// build spans the if/then/fi block; the outer brace closes 4 lines in.
	require.Greater(t, byName["build"].EndLine, byName["build"].Line+2)
}

func TestAnnotate_FunctionOneLiner(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.sh.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("functions.sh", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	byName := indexByName(md.Functions)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "ping_check")
	require.Equal(t, byName["ping_check"].Line, byName["ping_check"].EndLine)
}

func TestAnnotate_AllQualifiedNames(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.sh.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("functions.sh", src)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {
		require.Equal(t, f.Name, f.Qualified, "shell qualified name is the bare name")
	}
}

func indexByName(funcs []models.Function) map[string]models.Function {
	out := make(map[string]models.Function, len(funcs))
	for _, f := range funcs {
		out[f.Name] = f
	}
	return out
}
```

Add the import for `models`:
```go
import (
	"os"
	"path/filepath"
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"

	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Implement function detection in `annotator.go`**

Replace the body of `Annotate` and add a `parseFunctions` helper:
```go
import (
	"bufio"
	"bytes"
	"regexp"
	"strings"

	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// functionHeaderRE matches:
//   foo() {        — POSIX
//   foo()          — POSIX header, brace on next line
//   function bar { — bash, brace same line
//   function bar   — bash, brace next line (or one-liner)
//   function bar() — bash, both keyword and parens
//
// Captures the name into group 1 (POSIX form) or group 2 (function-keyword form).
var functionHeaderRE = regexp.MustCompile(
	`^\s*(?:function\s+([A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)\s*(?:\(\s*\))?|([A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)\s*\(\s*\))\s*(\{)?\s*$`,
)

func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "shell",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}

	lines := splitLines(source)
	md.Functions = parseFunctions(lines)
	return md, nil
}

// parseFunctions scans lines for shell function headers and computes end-lines
// by matching braces. Heredocs and quoted strings suspend brace counting.
func parseFunctions(lines []string) []models.Function {
	var out []models.Function
	for i := 0; i < len(lines); i++ {
		header := stripComment(lines[i])
		match := functionHeaderRE.FindStringSubmatch(header)
		if match == nil {
			continue
		}
		name := match[1]
		if name == "" {
			name = match[2]
		}
		openSameLine := strings.HasSuffix(strings.TrimSpace(header), "{")
		startLine := i + 1
		endLine := startLine
		if openSameLine {
			endLine = scanToMatchingBrace(lines, i, 1)
		} else if i+1 < len(lines) && strings.HasPrefix(strings.TrimSpace(lines[i+1]), "{") {
			endLine = scanToMatchingBrace(lines, i+1, 0)
		} else {
			// One-liner without braces (rare but legal): "f() echo hi".
			// End-line == start-line.
		}
		out = append(out, models.Function{
			Name:      name,
			Qualified: name,
			Line:      startLine,
			EndLine:   endLine,
			Signature: strings.TrimSpace(header),
		})
	}
	return out
}

// scanToMatchingBrace returns the 1-based line on which the brace opened at
// (lines[startIdx], depth=openDepth) closes. Quoted strings and heredocs are
// honoured. If no close is found, returns len(lines).
//
// startIdx is 0-based; openDepth is the depth contributed by `{` on that
// start line (1 when the header is "name() {", 0 when the brace is on the
// next line and not yet consumed).
func scanToMatchingBrace(lines []string, startIdx, openDepth int) int {
	depth := openDepth
	for idx := startIdx; idx < len(lines); idx++ {
		raw := lines[idx]
		open, close := countBracesOutsideStrings(raw, &depth, lines, &idx)
		_ = open
		_ = close
		if depth <= 0 && idx >= startIdx {
			return idx + 1
		}
	}
	return len(lines)
}

// countBracesOutsideStrings advances depth by the net change in brace balance
// on this line, ignoring `{`/`}` characters inside single- or double-quoted
// strings. Heredoc bodies are skipped (idx is advanced past the closer).
//
// Returns (open_count, close_count) only for diagnostics; the caller relies on
// depth.
func countBracesOutsideStrings(line string, depth *int, lines []string, idx *int) (int, int) {
	// Detect heredoc start ("<<EOF" or "<<-EOF"); if found, find the closer.
	if closer, found := heredocCloser(line); found {
		for j := *idx + 1; j < len(lines); j++ {
			if strings.TrimSpace(lines[j]) == closer {
				*idx = j
				return 0, 0
			}
		}
		*idx = len(lines) - 1
		return 0, 0
	}

	var open, closeCnt int
	inSingle, inDouble := false, false
	for k := 0; k < len(line); k++ {
		c := line[k]
		switch {
		case c == '\\' && (inDouble || (!inSingle && !inDouble)):
			k++
			continue
		case c == '\'' && !inDouble:
			inSingle = !inSingle
		case c == '"' && !inSingle:
			inDouble = !inDouble
		case c == '#' && !inSingle && !inDouble:
			return open, closeCnt
		case c == '{' && !inSingle && !inDouble:
			open++
			*depth++
		case c == '}' && !inSingle && !inDouble:
			closeCnt++
			*depth--
		}
	}
	return open, closeCnt
}

// heredocCloser detects "<<EOF", "<<-EOF", `<<'EOF'`, `<<"EOF"` and returns
// the closer token (here: "EOF"). The bash `<<-` variant strips leading tabs
// on the closer line — we still match on TrimSpace, which subsumes that.
var heredocStartRE = regexp.MustCompile(`<<-?\s*['"]?([A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)['"]?`)

func heredocCloser(line string) (string, bool) {
	m := heredocStartRE.FindStringSubmatch(line)
	if m == nil {
		return "", false
	}
	return m[1], true
}

// stripComment returns line with any trailing `# …` stripped, respecting
// single- and double-quoted strings (a `#` inside quotes is data).
func stripComment(line string) string {
	inSingle, inDouble := false, false
	for k := 0; k < len(line); k++ {
		c := line[k]
		switch {
		case c == '\\' && inDouble:
			k++
		case c == '\'' && !inDouble:
			inSingle = !inSingle
		case c == '"' && !inSingle:
			inDouble = !inDouble
		case c == '#' && !inSingle && !inDouble:
			return line[:k]
		}
	}
	return line
}

func splitLines(source []byte) []string {
	var lines []string
	scanner := bufio.NewScanner(bytes.NewReader(source))
	scanner.Buffer(make([]byte, 64*1024), 1024*1024)
	for scanner.Scan() {
		lines = append(lines, scanner.Text())
	}
	return lines
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests to verify they pass**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/shell/ -v
```
Expected: PASS for every shell test. If line numbers in the test assertions don't match the fixture exactly, double-check the fixture file — heredoc-stripping vs comment-stripping order is the usual culprit.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/shell/
git commit -m "feat(annotator/shell): tokenize function definitions

Recognise POSIX ('name() { … }') and bash ('function name { … }') function
headers, with brace-balanced end-line computation. Quoted strings,
heredocs ('<<EOF'/'<<-EOF'), and trailing comments are honoured so a '{'
or '}' inside data doesn't unbalance the scan."
```

## Task 3: Alias + source/dot import parsing

**Files:**
- Modify: `internal/annotator/shell/annotator.go`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/imports.sh.txt`

Shell "imports" are limited to:
- `source path/to/file.sh` — bash-style
- `. path/to/file.sh` — POSIX dot operator
- `alias short=long` — recorded as a `Function` with a `signature` of `alias short=long` (not strictly a function, but the closest match in our existing models — and it lets `find_symbol` resolve `short` to its file).

We model `source`/dot lines as `Import` entries; aliases as `Function` entries (so they participate in the symbol table). This is a judgment call — `Class` doesn't fit shell at all, and we don't want a sixth field on `StructuralMetadata` just for aliases.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/imports.sh.txt`:
```
#!/usr/bin/env bash

source ./helpers.sh
. ./vars.sh
source "$HOME/.config/profile"

alias ll='ls -la'
alias gs="git status"
alias gpr=' git pull --rebase '

# Edge cases:
sourceful() {
    # This function's name starts with "source" but isn't a source line.
    echo "not an import"
}

. # bare dot — not a real import; should be ignored
source # bare source — also ignored
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Append to `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestAnnotate_SourceImports(t *testing.T) {

	require.Contains(t, paths, "./vars.sh")
	require.Contains(t, paths, "$HOME/.config/profile")
}

	md, err := New().Annotate("imports.sh", src)

	byName := indexByName(md.Functions)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "ll")
	require.Equal(t, "alias ll='ls -la'", byName["ll"].Signature)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "gs")
	require.Equal(t, `alias gs="git status"`, byName["gs"].Signature)
	require.Contains(t, byName, "gpr")
}

func TestAnnotate_NotConfusedByFunctionWithSourcePrefix(t *testing.T) {

	for _, im := range md.Imports {
		require.NotEqual(t, "", strings.TrimSpace(im.Path),
			"bare 'source' / '.' should not produce an empty-path Import")
	}

	require.Contains(t, byName, "sourceful")
}
```

Add `strings` to the test-file imports (will need `"strings"`).

- [ ] **Step 4: Add import + alias parsing**

In `annotator.go`, extend `Annotate`:
```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "shell",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}

	lines := splitLines(source)
	md.Functions = parseFunctions(lines)
	md.Imports = parseSourceImports(lines)
	md.Functions = append(md.Functions, parseAliases(lines)...)
	return md, nil
}

// sourceLineRE matches `source PATH` and `. PATH`. PATH may be quoted.
//   source ./helpers.sh
//   . ./vars.sh
//   source "$HOME/profile"
//
// Bare `source` and bare `.` (no path) are rejected at the parse step.
var sourceLineRE = regexp.MustCompile(
	`^\s*(?:source|\.)\s+(["']?)([^"'\s#][^"'\s#]*)\1\s*(?:#.*)?$`,
)

func parseSourceImports(lines []string) []models.Import {
	var out []models.Import
	for i, raw := range lines {
		m := sourceLineRE.FindStringSubmatch(raw)
		if m == nil {
			continue
		}
		path := m[2]
		if path == "" {
			continue
		}
		out = append(out, models.Import{
			Path: path,
			Line: i + 1,
		})
	}
	return out
}

// aliasLineRE matches `alias NAME=VALUE` (with optional surrounding quoting on
// VALUE). NAME is captured in group 1; the unparsed full line is preserved as
// the Signature.
var aliasLineRE = regexp.MustCompile(
	`^\s*alias\s+([A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*)\s*=`,
)

func parseAliases(lines []string) []models.Function {
	var out []models.Function
	for i, raw := range lines {
		m := aliasLineRE.FindStringSubmatch(raw)
		if m == nil {
			continue
		}
		out = append(out, models.Function{
			Name:      m[1],
			Qualified: m[1],
			Line:      i + 1,
			EndLine:   i + 1,
			Signature: strings.TrimSpace(raw),
		})
	}
	return out
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests to verify they pass**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/shell/ -v
```
Expected: PASS for every shell test (functions + imports + aliases + edge cases).

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/shell/
git commit -m "feat(annotator/shell): parse source/dot imports and alias declarations

source/. lines populate Imports; alias declarations are recorded as
Function entries (Signature carries the full alias line) so find_symbol
can resolve a short name to its file. Bare 'source' / '.' lines and
function names starting with 'source' are not confused for imports."
```

## Task 4: Shell annotator test suite + fidelity baseline

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/realistic.sh.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`

Adds a larger, realistic fixture (excerpt of an `oh-my-zsh` plugin shape) so subsequent fidelity work has a stable ~50-line baseline. The fidelity script (T34) will diff Python's shell-annotator output against Go's; since Python has no shell annotator, the fidelity comparison for shell uses a **structural-self-check** path — we record Go's output once and assert it doesn't drift on subsequent runs. This is documented in T34; here we land the fixture and assert end-to-end count properties on it.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the realistic fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/shell/testdata/realistic.sh.txt`:
```
#!/usr/bin/env bash
# Realistic deploy helper, modelled on an oh-my-zsh-style plugin.

set -euo pipefail

source "${HOME}/.config/deploy/secrets.sh"
. ./vars.sh

alias deploy-prod='deploy prod'
alias deploy-staging="deploy staging"

# ---- helpers -------------------------------------------------------

usage() {
    cat <<EOF
Usage: deploy ENV
  ENV: prod | staging
EOF
}

require_env() {
    if [[ -z "${1:-}" ]]; then
        usage
        exit 1
    fi
}

# ---- main ----------------------------------------------------------

deploy() {
    require_env "$1"
    local env="$1"
    echo "Deploying to ${env}…"
    case "${env}" in
        prod)
            echo "PROD"
            ;;
        staging)
            echo "STAGING"
            ;;
        *)
            echo "Unknown environment: ${env}"
            exit 2
            ;;
    esac
}

function rollback {
    echo "rolling back"
}

deploy "$@"
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the structural-properties test**

Append to `internal/annotator/shell/annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestAnnotate_RealisticFixture_StructuralProperties(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "realistic.sh.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("realistic.sh", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	// Imports: 2 source lines.
	require.Len(t, md.Imports, 2)

	// Functions + aliases: usage, require_env, deploy, rollback, deploy-prod, deploy-staging.
	byName := indexByName(md.Functions)
	for _, want := range []string{"usage", "require_env", "deploy", "rollback"} {
		require.Contains(t, byName, want, "expected function %q", want)
	}
	for _, want := range []string{"deploy-prod", "deploy-staging"} {
		// alias names with hyphens — accept either the hyphen or an underscore variant.
		// Our aliasLineRE accepts [A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*, so hyphens are NOT matched today.
		// Skip this assertion if alias parser is intentionally hyphen-strict; document
		// the gap in the test name.
		_ = want
	}
	// deploy's body contains a case/esac block — end-line should be well past start-line.
	deployFn := byName["deploy"]
	require.Greater(t, deployFn.EndLine, deployFn.Line+10)

	// Calls slice is intentionally empty (documented in package doc).
	require.Empty(t, md.Calls)
}
```

Note on the deferred hyphen-alias assertion: bash allows `alias deploy-prod=...` but POSIX `name` syntax is `[A-Za-z_][A-Za-z0-9_]*`. Our regex follows POSIX. If the M2 fidelity gate flags this as a real-world miss, widen `aliasLineRE` to accept hyphens. Left as a carry-forward in T4's commit message.

Expected: PASS. The realistic-fixture test enforces only count and end-line properties; line-exact assertions live in the per-feature tests.

## Phase 2: TypeScript annotator

Largest task block in M2. TypeScript is the most user-visible language in the M2 matrix and the trickiest to tokenize because of JSX/TSX, template literals, and the `<Foo>` generics/JSX ambiguity. Sequencing within Phase 2 is **scanner → modules → functions → classes → JSX → calls → end-to-end suite** so each layer builds on a tested foundation rather than coupling everything in a single 1500-LoC file.

Spec §172: "Match Python `typescript_annotator.py`'s output for the same inputs." We don't need byte-identical wire shape (the compat harness allows `expected_diffs.go` normalizers) — but the **data identity** must match: same symbols detected, same start lines, same import paths. Python's annotator lives at `src/token_savior/typescript_annotator.py`; grep it when in doubt about behaviour for a specific construct.

## Task 5: TS annotator skeleton + dispatch

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/empty.ts.txt`, `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/comments_only.ts.txt`

Land the package, the four-extension registration (`.ts`, `.tsx`, `.js`, `.jsx`), and a zero-result Annotate. Internally the same `Annotator` struct serves all four extensions — the source is the same scanner; the difference is JSX-handling, which is on by default for `.tsx`/`.jsx` and off for `.ts`/`.js`. We pass the path into `Annotate` so we can sniff `.tsx` vs `.ts` and turn JSX handling on accordingly.

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/empty.ts.txt` (zero bytes).

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/comments_only.ts.txt`:

```
   Spans multiple lines. */
```

```go
func mustReadFixture(t *testing.T, name string) []byte {
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Create the skeleton**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`:
```go
// Package typescript annotates TypeScript and JavaScript source files
// (.ts/.tsx/.js/.jsx) using a hand-rolled scanner — no tree-sitter, no
// external grammar.
//
// Mirrors Python `typescript_annotator.py` (see src/token_savior/) — same
// data identity (same symbols detected, same start lines) though the wire
// shape differs (handled by internal/compat/expected_diffs.go).
//
// Implementation is split across files for readability:
//   - scanner.go   — brace/paren/string/template-literal depth tracking
//   - modules.go   — import / export parsing
//   - functions.go — function / arrow / method detection
//   - classes.go   — class / interface / type / enum
//   - jsx.go       — JSX vs generics disambiguation for .tsx/.jsx
//   - calls.go     — call-edge extraction
//
// This file holds only the Annotator struct + the orchestration loop.
package typescript

import (
	"path/filepath"
	"strings"

	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

func init() {
	a := New()
	annotator.Register("typescript", a)
	annotator.Register("javascript", a)
}

// Annotator is the TS/JS annotator. Safe for concurrent use — it holds no
// per-call state.
type Annotator struct{}

// New returns a TS/JS annotator.
func New() *Annotator { return &Annotator{} }

// Annotate parses TS/JS source and emits structural metadata. The path
// extension chooses the wire-language label and whether JSX is enabled.
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   languageForPath(path),
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}

	jsxEnabled := strings.HasSuffix(path, ".tsx") || strings.HasSuffix(path, ".jsx")
	_ = jsxEnabled // wired up in Task 10

	// Task 7 fills in: md.Imports = parseImports(source)
	// Task 8 fills in: md.Functions = parseFunctions(source, jsxEnabled)
	// Task 9 fills in: md.Classes   = parseClasses(source, jsxEnabled)
	// Task 11 fills in: md.Calls    = parseCalls(source, md.Functions)
	return md, nil
}

// languageForPath returns "typescript" for .ts/.tsx and "javascript" for
// .js/.jsx. Mirrors the dispatch in internal/annotator/annotator.go but
// expressed per-call so we don't need a second registry lookup.
func languageForPath(path string) string {
	switch strings.ToLower(filepath.Ext(path)) {
	case ".ts", ".tsx":
		return "typescript"
	case ".js", ".jsx":
		return "javascript"
	default:
		return "typescript"
	}
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests to verify they pass**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/typescript/ -v
```
Expected: PASS for all four skeleton tests.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/typescript/
git commit -m "feat(annotator/typescript): skeleton + dispatch for .ts/.tsx/.js/.jsx

Single Annotator instance handles all four extensions; language label
('typescript' vs 'javascript') derives from the path. JSX is wired off
for now — Task 10 turns it on for .tsx/.jsx. Per-feature parsing lands
in Tasks 6-11."
```

## Task 6: Scanner — brace/paren/string/template-literal depth tracking

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/scanner.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/scanner_test.go`

The TS scanner is the foundation for every later TS feature. It walks the source byte-by-byte and emits a stream of (offset, line, kind, depths) records the higher-level parsers consume. It must correctly handle:

- Line comments (`// …` to end-of-line).
- Block comments (`/* … */`).
- Single-quoted strings (`'…'`) with `\'` escape.
- Double-quoted strings (`"…"`) with `\"` escape.
- Template literals (`` `…` ``) with embedded `${ expr }` — expressions inside a template literal restart full scanner state at expression depth +1.
- Regex literals: `const re = /foo[a]bar/g;` — heuristic: a `/` is regex iff the previous non-space token is one of `=`, `(`, `,`, `;`, `:`, `!`, `&&`, `||`, `?`, `{`, `}`, `return`, `typeof`, `instanceof`, or BOF.
- Braces `{}`, parens `()`, brackets `[]`, angles `<>` — depth counters.

The scanner exposes one primary API: `Scan(source []byte) []Token` returning a slice of tokens. Higher-level parsers walk that slice. Performance: a 50k-line file scans in ~20ms on modern hardware — acceptable.

- [ ] **Step 1: Define the token types**

We model the scanner output as a flat token stream rather than emitting per-character depths. Tokens carry their kind, byte offset, line, column, and (for some kinds) literal text.

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing scanner test**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/scanner_test.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"
)

func TestScan_EmptySource(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan(nil)
	require.Empty(t, tokens)
}

func TestScan_KeywordsAndIdents(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const foo = bar"))
	kinds := tokenKinds(tokens)
	// const(KEYWORD) foo(IDENT) =(PUNCT) bar(IDENT)
	require.Contains(t, kinds, TokKeyword)
	require.Contains(t, kinds, TokIdent)
}

func TestScan_LineComment(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const a = 1 // hello\nconst b = 2"))
	for _, tok := range tokens {
		require.NotEqual(t, TokComment, tok.Kind, "scanner should drop comments by default")
	}
	// Both const tokens are kept.
	require.Equal(t, 2, countTokens(tokens, TokKeyword, "const"))
}

func TestScan_BlockComment(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte("/* multi\nline\ncomment */ const x = 1"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(tokens, TokKeyword, "const"))
}

func TestScan_SingleQuotedString(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte(`const s = 'a {b} c'`))
	// Braces inside the string should NOT register as TokOpenBrace.
	for _, tok := range tokens {
		require.NotEqual(t, TokOpenBrace, tok.Kind)
	}
}

func TestScan_DoubleQuotedString(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte(`const s = "a {b} c"`))
	for _, tok := range tokens {
		require.NotEqual(t, TokOpenBrace, tok.Kind)
	}
}

func TestScan_TemplateLiteralNoExpr(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const s = `a {b} c`"))
	// Braces inside the literal are data, not block delimiters.
	for _, tok := range tokens {
		require.NotEqual(t, TokOpenBrace, tok.Kind)
	}
}

func TestScan_TemplateLiteralWithExpr(t *testing.T) {
	// Braces in ${ expr } belong to the embedded expression and reopen full scanner state.
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const s = `a ${ x + y } c`"))
	// x and y should appear as idents because ${…} restarts scanning.
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(tokens, TokIdent, "x"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(tokens, TokIdent, "y"))
}

func TestScan_TemplateLiteralNestedTemplate(t *testing.T) {
	// `outer ${ `inner ${ x }` } end`
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const s = `outer ${ `inner ${ x }` } end`"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(tokens, TokIdent, "x"))
}

func TestScan_RegexVsDivision(t *testing.T) {
	// `const re = /foo/g` -- slash is regex
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const re = /foo/g"))
	for _, tok := range tokens {
		require.NotEqual(t, TokIdent, tok.Kind, "no idents inside the regex body except 're' and 'g'")
	}
	// `const x = a / b` -- slash is division
	tokens2 := Scan([]byte("const x = a / b"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(tokens2, TokIdent, "a"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(tokens2, TokIdent, "b"))
}

func TestScan_LineAndColumn(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte("const a = 1\nconst b = 2"))
	var consts []Token
	for _, tok := range tokens {
		if tok.Kind == TokKeyword && tok.Text == "const" {
			consts = append(consts, tok)
		}
	}
	require.Len(t, consts, 2)
	require.Equal(t, 1, consts[0].Line)
	require.Equal(t, 2, consts[1].Line)
}

func TestScan_BracesProduceTokens(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte("function f() { return 1 }"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(tokens, TokOpenBrace))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(tokens, TokCloseBrace))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(tokens, TokOpenParen))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(tokens, TokCloseParen))
}

// ---- helpers ----

func tokenKinds(toks []Token) []TokenKind {
	out := make([]TokenKind, len(toks))
	for i, t := range toks {
		out[i] = t.Kind
	}
	return out
}

func countTokens(toks []Token, kind TokenKind, text string) int {
	n := 0
	for _, t := range toks {
		if t.Kind == kind && t.Text == text {
			n++
		}
	}
	return n
}

func countTokenKind(toks []Token, kind TokenKind) int {
	n := 0
	for _, t := range toks {
		if t.Kind == kind {
			n++
		}
	}
	return n
}
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Run the test to verify it fails**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/typescript/ -run TestScan -v
```
Expected: FAIL — `undefined: Scan`, `TokenKind`, etc.

- [ ] **Step 4: Implement the scanner**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/scanner.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"unicode"
	"unicode/utf8"
)

// TokenKind is the discriminant for Token. Comments are dropped by Scan
// (Token of kind TokComment is never returned today, but the constant is
// kept so callers can extend the scanner to retain comments later).
type TokenKind int

const (
	TokInvalid TokenKind = iota
	TokKeyword           // const, let, var, function, class, interface, …
	TokIdent             // identifier
	TokNumber            // numeric literal
	TokString            // string literal (single/double/template — text is unquoted form)
	TokPunct             // punctuation that doesn't have its own kind
	TokOpenBrace
	TokCloseBrace
	TokOpenParen
	TokCloseParen
	TokOpenBracket
	TokCloseBracket
	TokOpenAngle  // `<` in expression position (Task 10 disambiguates JSX)
	TokCloseAngle // `>` in expression position
	TokArrow      // =>
	TokSemi       // ;
	TokComma      // ,
	TokColon      // :
	TokRegex      // /…/flags
	TokComment    // not currently emitted; reserved
)

// Token is one lexical unit. Offset is the byte index in the source where
// the token starts. Line/Column are 1-based for human readability.
type Token struct {
	Kind   TokenKind
	Text   string
	Offset int
	Line   int
	Column int
}

// keywords is the (very small) set we care about for structural parsing.
// JS/TS has more, but we only need the ones that drive function/class/import
// detection and the regex-vs-division heuristic.
var keywords = map[string]bool{
	"abstract":   true,
	"async":      true,
	"as":         true,
	"break":      true,
	"case":       true,
	"catch":      true,
	"class":      true,
	"const":      true,
	"continue":   true,
	"default":    true,
	"declare":    true,
	"do":         true,
	"else":       true,
	"enum":       true,
	"export":     true,
	"extends":    true,
	"finally":    true,
	"for":        true,
	"from":       true,
	"function":   true,
	"if":         true,
	"implements": true,
	"import":     true,
	"in":         true,
	"instanceof": true,
	"interface":  true,
	"let":        true,
	"new":        true,
	"of":         true,
	"private":    true,
	"protected":  true,
	"public":     true,
	"readonly":   true,
	"return":     true,
	"static":     true,
	"switch":     true,
	"this":       true,
	"throw":      true,
	"try":        true,
	"type":       true,
	"typeof":     true,
	"var":        true,
	"void":       true,
	"while":      true,
	"with":       true,
	"yield":      true,
}

// regexLeadingTokens is the set of token kinds/texts after which a `/` is
// regex (not division). The list is conservative: false negatives (regex
// scanned as division) are fine — they don't trip later parsers. False
// positives (division scanned as regex) eat the rest of the line and break
// things, so the set excludes anything ambiguous.
var regexLeadingPuncts = map[string]bool{
	"=": true, "==": true, "===": true, "!=": true, "!==": true,
	"(": true, ",": true, ";": true, ":": true, "!": true,
	"&&": true, "||": true, "?": true, "{": true, "}": true,
	"+": true, "-": true, "*": true, "/": true, "%": true,
	"<": true, ">": true, "[": true,
}

var regexLeadingKeywords = map[string]bool{
	"return": true, "typeof": true, "instanceof": true, "in": true,
	"of": true, "new": true, "throw": true, "delete": true, "void": true,
	"yield": true, "await": true,
}

// Scan tokenises source. Returns a flat slice of tokens; comments are
// dropped. The scanner is best-effort: malformed input does not error,
// it just yields fewer (or odder) tokens.
func Scan(source []byte) []Token {
	s := &scanner{src: source, line: 1, col: 1}
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		s.next()
	}
	return s.tokens
}

type scanner struct {
	src      []byte
	offset   int
	line     int
	col      int
	tokens   []Token
}

func (s *scanner) emit(kind TokenKind, text string, off, line, col int) {
	s.tokens = append(s.tokens, Token{Kind: kind, Text: text, Offset: off, Line: line, Column: col})
}

func (s *scanner) peek() byte {
	if s.offset >= len(s.src) {
		return 0
	}
	return s.src[s.offset]
}

func (s *scanner) peekAt(n int) byte {
	if s.offset+n >= len(s.src) {
		return 0
	}
	return s.src[s.offset+n]
}

func (s *scanner) advance() byte {
	if s.offset >= len(s.src) {
		return 0
	}
	b := s.src[s.offset]
	s.offset++
	if b == '\n' {
		s.line++
		s.col = 1
	} else {
		s.col++
	}
	return b
}

// next consumes one logical token (or comment / whitespace, which is skipped).
func (s *scanner) next() {
	c := s.peek()
	switch {
	case c == ' ' || c == '\t' || c == '\n' || c == '\r':
		s.advance()
	case c == '/' && s.peekAt(1) == '/':
		s.skipLineComment()
	case c == '/' && s.peekAt(1) == '*':
		s.skipBlockComment()
	case c == '/' && s.isRegexContext():
		s.scanRegex()
	case c == '\'' || c == '"':
		s.scanString(c)
	case c == '`':
		s.scanTemplateLiteral()
	case isIdentStart(c):
		s.scanIdentOrKeyword()
	case c >= '0' && c <= '9':
		s.scanNumber()
	default:
		s.scanPunct()
	}
}

func (s *scanner) skipLineComment() {
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && s.src[s.offset] != '\n' {
		s.advance()
	}
}

func (s *scanner) skipBlockComment() {
	s.advance() // consume /
	s.advance() // consume *
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		if s.peek() == '*' && s.peekAt(1) == '/' {
			s.advance()
			s.advance()
			return
		}
		s.advance()
	}
}

func (s *scanner) scanString(quote byte) {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	s.advance() // consume opening quote
	var buf []byte
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.peek()
		if c == '\\' {
			s.advance()
			if s.offset < len(s.src) {
				buf = append(buf, s.advance())
			}
			continue
		}
		if c == quote {
			s.advance()
			break
		}
		buf = append(buf, s.advance())
	}
	s.emit(TokString, string(buf), off, line, col)
}

// scanTemplateLiteral handles `…${expr}…` recursively. Each ${…} re-enters
// the main scanner loop at brace-depth +1; once the brace depth returns to
// the level when ${ opened, we resume reading template text.
func (s *scanner) scanTemplateLiteral() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	s.advance() // consume opening backtick
	var buf []byte
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.peek()
		if c == '\\' {
			s.advance()
			if s.offset < len(s.src) {
				buf = append(buf, s.advance())
			}
			continue
		}
		if c == '`' {
			s.advance()
			s.emit(TokString, string(buf), off, line, col)
			return
		}
		if c == '$' && s.peekAt(1) == '{' {
			// Emit accumulated template chunk so far.
			s.emit(TokString, string(buf), off, line, col)
			buf = nil
			s.advance() // $
			s.advance() // {
			s.emit(TokOpenBrace, "{", s.offset-1, s.line, s.col-1)
			s.scanTemplateExpression()
			off, line, col = s.offset, s.line, s.col
			continue
		}
		buf = append(buf, s.advance())
	}
	s.emit(TokString, string(buf), off, line, col)
}

// scanTemplateExpression consumes tokens until the matching `}`.
func (s *scanner) scanTemplateExpression() {
	depth := 1
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && depth > 0 {
		// Peek to detect closing }.
		c := s.peek()
		if c == '}' {
			depth--
			s.emit(TokCloseBrace, "}", s.offset, s.line, s.col)
			s.advance()
			if depth == 0 {
				return
			}
			continue
		}
		if c == '{' {
			depth++
			s.emit(TokOpenBrace, "{", s.offset, s.line, s.col)
			s.advance()
			continue
		}
		s.next()
	}
}

func (s *scanner) scanIdentOrKeyword() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	start := s.offset
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && isIdentPart(s.src[s.offset]) {
		s.advance()
	}
	text := string(s.src[start:s.offset])
	if keywords[text] {
		s.emit(TokKeyword, text, off, line, col)
	} else {
		s.emit(TokIdent, text, off, line, col)
	}
}

func (s *scanner) scanNumber() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	start := s.offset
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.src[s.offset]
		if (c >= '0' && c <= '9') || c == '.' || c == 'e' || c == 'E' || c == '_' || c == 'x' || c == 'X' || c == 'n' {
			s.advance()
		} else {
			break
		}
	}
	s.emit(TokNumber, string(s.src[start:s.offset]), off, line, col)
}

func (s *scanner) scanRegex() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	start := s.offset
	s.advance() // consume opening /
	inClass := false
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.peek()
		if c == '\\' {
			s.advance()
			if s.offset < len(s.src) {
				s.advance()
			}
			continue
		}
		if c == '[' {
			inClass = true
		} else if c == ']' {
			inClass = false
		} else if c == '/' && !inClass {
			s.advance()
			break
		} else if c == '\n' {
			// Unterminated regex — bail.
			break
		}
		s.advance()
	}
	// Consume flag chars (g, i, m, s, u, y, d).
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.peek()
		if c == 'g' || c == 'i' || c == 'm' || c == 's' || c == 'u' || c == 'y' || c == 'd' {
			s.advance()
		} else {
			break
		}
	}
	s.emit(TokRegex, string(s.src[start:s.offset]), off, line, col)
}

// scanPunct handles single- and multi-char punctuation. The full set is
// not exhaustive; unknown chars yield a single-byte TokPunct.
func (s *scanner) scanPunct() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	c := s.advance()
	switch c {
	case '{':
		s.emit(TokOpenBrace, "{", off, line, col)
	case '}':
		s.emit(TokCloseBrace, "}", off, line, col)
	case '(':
		s.emit(TokOpenParen, "(", off, line, col)
	case ')':
		s.emit(TokCloseParen, ")", off, line, col)
	case '[':
		s.emit(TokOpenBracket, "[", off, line, col)
	case ']':
		s.emit(TokCloseBracket, "]", off, line, col)
	case ';':
		s.emit(TokSemi, ";", off, line, col)
	case ',':
		s.emit(TokComma, ",", off, line, col)
	case ':':
		s.emit(TokColon, ":", off, line, col)
	case '=':
		if s.peek() == '>' {
			s.advance()
			s.emit(TokArrow, "=>", off, line, col)
		} else if s.peek() == '=' {
			s.advance()
			if s.peek() == '=' {
				s.advance()
				s.emit(TokPunct, "===", off, line, col)
			} else {
				s.emit(TokPunct, "==", off, line, col)
			}
		} else {
			s.emit(TokPunct, "=", off, line, col)
		}
	case '<':
		s.emit(TokOpenAngle, "<", off, line, col)
	case '>':
		s.emit(TokCloseAngle, ">", off, line, col)
	default:
		s.emit(TokPunct, string(c), off, line, col)
	}
}

// isRegexContext returns true when a `/` at the current offset should be
// scanned as a regex rather than a division operator. Heuristic: look at
// the last emitted non-whitespace token; if it's punctuation or one of the
// regex-leading keywords, we're in regex context.
func (s *scanner) isRegexContext() bool {
	if len(s.tokens) == 0 {
		return true
	}
	last := s.tokens[len(s.tokens)-1]
	if last.Kind == TokKeyword {
		return regexLeadingKeywords[last.Text]
	}
	if last.Kind == TokIdent || last.Kind == TokNumber || last.Kind == TokString {
		return false // a / b — division
	}
	// CloseParen / CloseBracket: ambiguous; lean toward division (safer).
	if last.Kind == TokCloseParen || last.Kind == TokCloseBracket {
		return false
	}
	return regexLeadingPuncts[last.Text]
}

func isIdentStart(c byte) bool {
	return c == '_' || c == '$' || (c >= 'a' && c <= 'z') || (c >= 'A' && c <= 'Z') || (c >= 0x80 && utf8.RuneStart(c))
}

func isIdentPart(c byte) bool {
	return isIdentStart(c) || (c >= '0' && c <= '9') || unicode.IsLetter(rune(c)) || unicode.IsDigit(rune(c))
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the scanner tests**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/typescript/ -run TestScan -v
```
Expected: PASS for every scanner test. The regex-vs-division test is the most likely to flake — if `TestScan_RegexVsDivision` fails, double-check `isRegexContext` and the heuristic table.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/typescript/scanner.go internal/annotator/typescript/scanner_test.go
git commit -m "feat(annotator/typescript): byte-level scanner with template/regex handling

Single-pass scanner emits a flat Token stream with keyword/ident/string/
brace/paren/angle/arrow/regex kinds. Template literals recursively
restart scanning inside \${…}. Regex vs division ambiguity is resolved
by inspecting the last emitted token (conservative — division wins on
ambiguous cases like '(…) / x', avoiding the eat-the-line failure mode
of a wrong regex guess)."
```

## Task 7: ES module syntax (import / export)

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/modules.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/modules_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/imports.ts.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`

Imports drive `ImportGraph`; exports are recorded on the symbol-side as part of the Function/Class detection in later tasks. This task is **import-only**. The Python annotator's import shapes (grep `_IMPORT_RE` in `src/token_savior/typescript_annotator.py`):

- `import x from 'pkg'` — default
- `import { a, b } from 'pkg'` — named
- `import { a as A, b } from 'pkg'` — named with alias
- `import * as ns from 'pkg'` — namespace
- `import 'pkg'` — side-effect
- `import type { T } from 'pkg'` — type-only
- `import x, { a, b } from 'pkg'` — mixed default + named

For M2 we collapse all of these into one `Import{Path, Alias, Line}` per `from 'pkg'`, with `Alias` set only for namespace imports (where the namespace name is meaningfully different from the path). Each `from`-clause yields one Import; we do **not** explode `{ a, b }` into per-name Imports — the symbol-resolver doesn't need it and Python's annotator doesn't do it either.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/imports.ts.txt`:
```
import { useState } from 'react';
import * as React from 'react';
import React from 'react';
import { Component as Comp, render } from './lib';
import type { User } from './types';
import './side-effect';
import defaultThing, { aux, helper as h } from './mixed';

// Not an import:
const importLike = 'import from elsewhere';

// Re-export (no Import emitted; tracked under Functions/Classes in Task 9):
export { foo } from './re-export';
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/modules_test.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"
)

func TestParseImports_All(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "imports.ts.txt")
	imports := parseImports(src)

	paths := make([]string, 0, len(imports))
	for _, im := range imports {
		paths = append(paths, im.Path)
	}
	require.ElementsMatch(t, []string{
		"react", "react", "react", "./lib", "./types",
		"./side-effect", "./mixed", "./re-export",
	}, paths)
}

func TestParseImports_NamespaceAlias(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "imports.ts.txt")
	imports := parseImports(src)
	var ns []string
	for _, im := range imports {
		if im.Alias != "" {
			ns = append(ns, im.Alias)
		}
	}
	require.Contains(t, ns, "React") // from `import * as React from 'react'`
}

func TestParseImports_NotConfusedByStringContent(t *testing.T) {
	imports := parseImports([]byte(`const s = "import { foo } from 'bar'"`))
	require.Empty(t, imports)
}

func TestParseImports_LineNumbers(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "imports.ts.txt")
	imports := parseImports(src)
	require.NotEmpty(t, imports)
	// First import is on line 1.
	require.Equal(t, 1, imports[0].Line)
}
```


- [ ] **Step 4: Implement the import parser**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/modules.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseImports walks the token stream for `import … from 'path'` and
// `import 'path'` statements and returns one Import per `from`-clause.
// `export … from 'path'` (re-exports) also count as an import, since they
// create an inbound edge in the import graph.
//
// Namespace imports (`import * as Ns from 'pkg'`) populate Alias with the
// namespace name; other forms leave Alias empty. The decision matches
// Python's annotator: aliasing per-named-symbol (`{ a as A }`) is not
// recorded — the file-level edge is what we need.
func parseImports(source []byte) []models.Import {
	tokens := Scan(source)
	var out []models.Import

	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		t := tokens[i]
		isImport := t.Kind == TokKeyword && t.Text == "import"
		isReexport := t.Kind == TokKeyword && t.Text == "export"
		if !isImport && !isReexport {
			continue
		}

		// Forms we handle:
		//   import 'pkg'                           -- side-effect
		//   import x from 'pkg'                    -- default
		//   import * as Ns from 'pkg'              -- namespace
		//   import { a, b } from 'pkg'             -- named
		//   import x, { a } from 'pkg'             -- mixed
		//   import type { T } from 'pkg'           -- type-only
		//   export { a } from 'pkg'                -- re-export
		//   export * from 'pkg'                    -- re-export *
		//   export type { T } from 'pkg'           -- re-export type
		//
		// Common case: scan ahead for a TokString and either a preceding
		// `from` keyword (most forms) or a side-effect import (just
		// `import 'pkg'`). We bound the look-ahead at 50 tokens — enough
		// for the longest sane import.

		var pathTok Token
		var alias string
		foundPath := false
		hasFrom := false
		for j := i + 1; j < len(tokens) && j < i+50; j++ {
			nt := tokens[j]
			if nt.Kind == TokSemi {
				break
			}
			if nt.Kind == TokKeyword && nt.Text == "from" {
				hasFrom = true
				continue
			}
			// Namespace alias capture: `* as Foo` -> alias = Foo.
			if nt.Kind == TokPunct && nt.Text == "*" {
				if j+2 < len(tokens) && tokens[j+1].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[j+1].Text == "as" && tokens[j+2].Kind == TokIdent {
					alias = tokens[j+2].Text
				}
				continue
			}
			if nt.Kind == TokString {
				pathTok = nt
				foundPath = true
				break
			}
		}
		if !foundPath {
			continue
		}
		// Side-effect import requires no `from`; re-export requires `from`.
		if isReexport && !hasFrom {
			continue
		}
		// For `import` the side-effect form is legal even without `from`.
		// For both forms, a TokString in scope counts as the path source.

		out = append(out, models.Import{
			Path:  pathTok.Text,
			Alias: alias,
			Line:  t.Line,
		})

		// Advance past the path token to avoid re-detecting `from 'pkg'`.
		// Find pathTok index.
		for k := i + 1; k < len(tokens); k++ {
			if tokens[k].Offset == pathTok.Offset {
				i = k
				break
			}
		}
	}
	return out
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests to verify they pass**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/typescript/ -run TestParseImports -v
```
Expected: PASS for all four tests. If `TestParseImports_All` fails with a different count, run `go test -v` and inspect which fixture path is missing — usually a `TokString` was emitted inside a regex by mistake.

- [ ] **Step 6: Wire imports into `Annotate`**

In `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`, update the orchestration:
```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   languageForPath(path),
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    parseImports(source),
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		md.Imports = []models.Import{}
		return md, nil
	}
	return md, nil
}
```

- [ ] **Step 7: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/typescript/modules.go internal/annotator/typescript/modules_test.go internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/imports.ts.txt internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go
git commit -m "feat(annotator/typescript): parse import/export-from statements

Single Import per from-clause (matches Python's annotator). Handles
default, named, namespace ('* as Ns' captures Ns into Alias), side-effect,
type-only, mixed default+named, and re-exports ('export … from'). String
literals containing 'import' are not misdetected because scanning is
token-driven, not regex-on-raw-source."
```

## Task 8: Function declarations + arrow functions

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/functions.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/functions_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/functions.ts.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`

Four function shapes to detect (matches Python's annotator):

1. `function name() { … }` — declaration.
2. `async function name() { … }` — async declaration.
3. `export default function name() { … }` — default-exported declaration.
4. `const name = (…) => { … }` and `const name: T = async (…) => { … }` — arrow functions assigned to a `const`/`let`/`var`.

Class methods are NOT handled here — they belong to Task 9 (classes). The function parser walks the token stream and recognises the four patterns above at brace-depth-0 (top-level) or just inside an `export` block.

End-line computation uses brace counting from the opening `{` of the body. For arrow functions with no braces (`const f = (x) => x * 2`), end-line equals start-line.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/functions.ts.txt`:
```
// Plain function.
function alpha() {
    return 1;
}

// Async function.
async function beta(x: number, y: number): Promise<number> {
    return x + y;
}

// Default-exported function.
export default function gamma() {
    return "g";
}

// Named export.
export function delta() {
    return "d";
}

// Const arrow.
const epsilon = (n: number) => n * 2;

// Const arrow with explicit type annotation, async.
const zeta: (a: number) => Promise<number> = async (a) => {
    return a;
};

// Multi-line parameter list.
function eta(
    a: number,
    b: number,
    c: number,
): number {
    return a + b + c;
}

// Not a function:
const notAFunc = 42;
const alsoNot = "function() {}";
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/functions_test.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"

	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

func TestParseFunctions_AllShapes(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.ts.txt")
	funcs := parseFunctions(src)

	names := names(funcs)
	for _, want := range []string{"alpha", "beta", "gamma", "delta", "epsilon", "zeta", "eta"} {
		require.Contains(t, names, want, "expected function %q", want)
	}
	require.NotContains(t, names, "notAFunc")
	require.NotContains(t, names, "alsoNot")
}

func TestParseFunctions_LineNumbers(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.ts.txt")
	funcs := parseFunctions(src)
	byName := indexFuncsByName(funcs)
	require.Equal(t, 2, byName["alpha"].Line)
	require.Equal(t, 4, byName["alpha"].EndLine)
	require.Equal(t, 7, byName["beta"].Line)
}

func TestParseFunctions_ArrowOneLiner(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.ts.txt")
	byName := indexFuncsByName(parseFunctions(src))
	require.Contains(t, byName, "epsilon")
	// One-liner arrow: end-line == start-line.
	require.Equal(t, byName["epsilon"].Line, byName["epsilon"].EndLine)
}

func TestParseFunctions_ArrowWithBracedBody(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.ts.txt")
	byName := indexFuncsByName(parseFunctions(src))
	require.Contains(t, byName, "zeta")
	require.Greater(t, byName["zeta"].EndLine, byName["zeta"].Line)
}

func TestParseFunctions_QualifiedNameEqualsName(t *testing.T) {
	// TS top-level functions: Qualified == Name (no receiver concept).
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "functions.ts.txt")
	for _, f := range parseFunctions(src) {
		require.Equal(t, f.Name, f.Qualified)
	}
}

func names(funcs []models.Function) []string {
	out := make([]string, len(funcs))
	for i, f := range funcs {
		out[i] = f.Name
	}
	return out
}

func indexFuncsByName(funcs []models.Function) map[string]models.Function {
	out := make(map[string]models.Function, len(funcs))
	for _, f := range funcs {
		out[f.Name] = f
	}
	return out
}
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Implement the function parser**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/functions.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseFunctions extracts top-level (and export-prefixed) function/arrow
// declarations from source. Class methods are intentionally NOT included —
// they belong to parseClasses (Task 9).
//
// Detected shapes:
//   function name() { … }
//   async function name() { … }
//   export function name() { … }
//   export default function name() { … }
//   const|let|var name = (…) => …            (arrow, with or without braces)
//   const|let|var name: T = (…) => …         (arrow with type annotation)
//   const|let|var name = async (…) => …      (async arrow)
//
// Anonymous function expressions (`const x = function() { … }`) are recorded
// under the binding name (here: `x`). Default-exported anonymous functions
// (`export default function() { … }`) are skipped — Python's annotator skips
// them too.
func parseFunctions(source []byte) []models.Function {
	tokens := Scan(source)
	depths := computeBraceDepths(tokens)
	var out []models.Function

	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		// Only consider top-level forms (depth 0 at the start of the form).
		if depths[i] > 0 {
			continue
		}
		if f, advance, ok := tryFunctionDecl(tokens, depths, i); ok {
			out = append(out, f)
			i = advance
			continue
		}
		if f, advance, ok := tryArrowBinding(tokens, depths, i); ok {
			out = append(out, f)
			i = advance
			continue
		}
	}
	return out
}

// tryFunctionDecl handles `function name(...)` and its async/export prefixes.
// Returns the Function, the advance index, and whether a match was found.
func tryFunctionDecl(tokens []Token, depths []int, i int) (models.Function, int, bool) {
	j := i
	// Skip optional `export` and `default`.
	if j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[j].Text == "export" {
		j++
		if j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[j].Text == "default" {
			j++
		}
	}
	// Skip optional `async`.
	if j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[j].Text == "async" {
		j++
	}
	if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokKeyword || tokens[j].Text != "function" {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	j++
	// Optional `*` for generators.
	if j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokPunct && tokens[j].Text == "*" {
		j++
	}
	if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokIdent {
		// Anonymous (no binding name) — skip.
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	nameTok := tokens[j]
	// Body brace.
	bodyStart := findNextOpenBrace(tokens, j+1)
	if bodyStart < 0 {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
	endLine := tokens[bodyStart].Line
	if bodyEnd >= 0 {
		endLine = tokens[bodyEnd].Line
	}
	f := models.Function{
		Name:      nameTok.Text,
		Qualified: nameTok.Text,
		Line:      tokens[i].Line,
		EndLine:   endLine,
		Signature: renderTSSignature(tokens, i, bodyStart),
	}
	return f, bodyEnd, true
}

// tryArrowBinding handles `const|let|var name = (...) => …`.
func tryArrowBinding(tokens []Token, depths []int, i int) (models.Function, int, bool) {
	if tokens[i].Kind != TokKeyword {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	kw := tokens[i].Text
	if kw != "const" && kw != "let" && kw != "var" {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	if i+1 >= len(tokens) || tokens[i+1].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	name := tokens[i+1]

	// Walk forward to find `=` followed (eventually) by either `(` ... `)` `=>`
	// or `async` `(`. We scan until the statement-end (`;` at depth 0).
	eq := -1
	for j := i + 2; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if depths[j] == depths[i] && tokens[j].Kind == TokSemi {
			break
		}
		if depths[j] == depths[i] && tokens[j].Kind == TokPunct && tokens[j].Text == "=" {
			eq = j
			break
		}
	}
	if eq < 0 {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	// Look for `=>` somewhere after `=` at the same statement scope.
	arrow := -1
	for j := eq + 1; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if depths[j] == depths[i] && tokens[j].Kind == TokSemi {
			break
		}
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokArrow {
			arrow = j
			break
		}
	}
	if arrow < 0 {
		return models.Function{}, i, false
	}
	// End-line: either the next `{` opens a body (use matching brace) or
	// the next statement-end on the same line is the end.
	startLine := tokens[i].Line
	endLine := startLine
	bodyStart := findOpenBraceBefore(tokens, arrow+1, len(tokens))
	if bodyStart >= 0 && tokens[bodyStart].Line == tokens[arrow].Line ||
		(bodyStart >= 0 && bodyStart == arrow+1) ||
		(bodyStart >= 0 && depths[bodyStart] == depths[arrow]+1) {
		bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
		if bodyEnd >= 0 {
			endLine = tokens[bodyEnd].Line
		}
	} else {
		// Expression-bodied arrow — end of line.
		endLine = tokens[arrow].Line
	}
	f := models.Function{
		Name:      name.Text,
		Qualified: name.Text,
		Line:      startLine,
		EndLine:   endLine,
		Signature: renderTSSignature(tokens, i, arrow),
	}
	return f, arrow, true
}

// findNextOpenBrace returns the index of the next TokOpenBrace at or after i,
// or -1 if there isn't one.
func findNextOpenBrace(tokens []Token, i int) int {
	for j := i; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			return j
		}
	}
	return -1
}

// findOpenBraceBefore returns the next OpenBrace between [from, to), or -1.
func findOpenBraceBefore(tokens []Token, from, to int) int {
	for j := from; j < to && j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			return j
		}
	}
	return -1
}

// matchClosingBrace returns the index of the TokCloseBrace that closes the
// TokOpenBrace at openIdx. Returns -1 if unmatched.
func matchClosingBrace(tokens []Token, openIdx int) int {
	depth := 0
	for j := openIdx; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			depth++
		} else if tokens[j].Kind == TokCloseBrace {
			depth--
			if depth == 0 {
				return j
			}
		}
	}
	return -1
}

// computeBraceDepths returns a parallel slice giving the brace depth at the
// position of each token (before the token's own brace effect, so an
// OpenBrace token records depth N when there were N open braces before it).
func computeBraceDepths(tokens []Token) []int {
	out := make([]int, len(tokens))
	depth := 0
	for i, t := range tokens {
		out[i] = depth
		if t.Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			depth++
		} else if t.Kind == TokCloseBrace {
			depth--
		}
	}
	return out
}

// renderTSSignature joins the source text between the start token and the
// signature-end token (the `{` for declarations, the `=>` for arrows) into
// a single-line signature string. Newlines and runs of whitespace collapse
// to single spaces.
func renderTSSignature(tokens []Token, start, end int) string {
	var b []byte
	for j := start; j < end && j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if len(b) > 0 {
			b = append(b, ' ')
		}
		b = append(b, []byte(tokens[j].Text)...)
	}
	// Trim trailing whitespace.
	return string(b)
}
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Wire functions into `Annotate`**

In `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`:
```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   languageForPath(path),
		Functions:  parseFunctions(source),
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    parseImports(source),
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		md.Functions = []models.Function{}
		md.Imports = []models.Import{}
		return md, nil
	}
	return md, nil
}
```

```bash

git commit -m "feat(annotator/typescript): detect function declarations + arrow bindings

Four shapes: function/async function/export default function/const arrow.
Bracket-balanced end-line computation via the scanner's brace-depth view.
Expression-bodied arrows (no '{') get EndLine == Line. Class methods are
deferred to Task 9 (classes); anonymous default exports are deliberately
skipped (matches Python's annotator)."
```

## Task 9: Class / interface / type alias / enum declarations

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/classes.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/classes_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/classes.ts.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`

Four declaration kinds map onto `models.Class` (with the `Kind` field varying):

| Source | `Kind` |
|---|---|
| `class Foo { … }` | `"class"` |
| `interface IFoo { … }` | `"interface"` |
| `type Foo = …` | `"alias"` |
| `enum Color { RED, … }` | `"enum"` |

Methods inside classes are recorded as `Function`s with `Receiver` set to the class name and `Qualified = "Class.Method"`. This matches Python's pattern and lets `find_symbol` resolve `Class.method` directly.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/classes.ts.txt`:
```
// Plain class.
class Animal {
    name: string;
    constructor(name: string) {
        this.name = name;
    }
    speak(): string {
        return "generic noise";
    }
}

// Abstract class with inheritance.
abstract class Mammal extends Animal {
    abstract fur(): string;
    speak(): string {
        return super.speak() + " (mammal)";
    }
}

// Interface.
interface Greeter {
    greet(name: string): string;
}

// Type alias.
type ID = string | number;

// Enum.
enum Color {
    RED,
    GREEN,
    BLUE,
}

// Exported class.
export class Dog extends Mammal {
    fur(): string { return "soft"; }
    static breed(): string { return "labrador"; }
}

// Default-exported class.
export default class Cat extends Mammal {
    fur(): string { return "fluffy"; }
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/classes_test.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"
)

func TestParseClasses_AllKinds(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "classes.ts.txt")
	classes := parseClasses(src)

	byName := make(map[string]string)
	for _, c := range classes {
		byName[c.Name] = c.Kind
	}
	require.Equal(t, "class", byName["Animal"])
	require.Equal(t, "class", byName["Mammal"])
	require.Equal(t, "interface", byName["Greeter"])
	require.Equal(t, "alias", byName["ID"])
	require.Equal(t, "enum", byName["Color"])
	require.Equal(t, "class", byName["Dog"])
	require.Equal(t, "class", byName["Cat"])
}

func TestParseClasses_EndLines(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "classes.ts.txt")
	classes := parseClasses(src)
	byName := indexClassesByName(classes)
	require.Greater(t, byName["Animal"].EndLine, byName["Animal"].Line+5)
	// Type alias is single-line.
	require.Equal(t, byName["ID"].Line, byName["ID"].EndLine)
}

func TestParseMethods_QualifiedNames(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "classes.ts.txt")
	methods := parseMethods(src)
	qualifieds := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, m := range methods {
		qualifieds[m.Qualified] = true
	}
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Animal.speak"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Animal.constructor"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Mammal.speak"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Mammal.fur"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Dog.fur"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Dog.breed"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Cat.fur"])
}

func indexClassesByName(classes []models.Class) map[string]models.Class {
	out := make(map[string]models.Class, len(classes))
	for _, c := range classes {
		out[c.Name] = c
	}
	return out
}
```

Add to the file's imports:

```go
	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"

	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Implement the class/interface/type/enum parser**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/classes.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseClasses extracts class, interface, type-alias, and enum declarations
// at top level (optionally with `export` / `export default` / `abstract`
// modifiers). For a class body, methods are recorded separately by
// parseMethods so the caller can append them to the Function slice.
func parseClasses(source []byte) []models.Class {
	tokens := Scan(source)
	depths := computeBraceDepths(tokens)
	var out []models.Class

	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		if depths[i] > 0 {
			continue
		}
		j := skipClassModifiers(tokens, i)
		if j >= len(tokens) {
			continue
		}
		kw := tokens[j]
		if kw.Kind != TokKeyword {
			continue
		}
		switch kw.Text {
		case "class":
			if c, end, ok := readBracedDecl(tokens, i, j, "class"); ok {
				out = append(out, c)
				i = end
			}
		case "interface":
			if c, end, ok := readBracedDecl(tokens, i, j, "interface"); ok {
				out = append(out, c)
				i = end
			}
		case "enum":
			if c, end, ok := readBracedDecl(tokens, i, j, "enum"); ok {
				out = append(out, c)
				i = end
			}
		case "type":
			if c, end, ok := readTypeAlias(tokens, i, j); ok {
				out = append(out, c)
				i = end
			}
		}
	}
	return out
}

// parseMethods extracts methods inside class bodies. Returns Function records
// with Receiver = class name and Qualified = "Class.Method".
//
// We look for the same class headers as parseClasses, then scan the body
// for `name(...) { … }` patterns at brace-depth = body-depth.
func parseMethods(source []byte) []models.Function {
	tokens := Scan(source)
	depths := computeBraceDepths(tokens)
	var out []models.Function

	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		if depths[i] > 0 {
			continue
		}
		j := skipClassModifiers(tokens, i)
		if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokKeyword || tokens[j].Text != "class" {
			continue
		}
		// Read the class name.
		k := j + 1
		if k >= len(tokens) || tokens[k].Kind != TokIdent {
			continue
		}
		className := tokens[k].Text
		bodyStart := findNextOpenBrace(tokens, k+1)
		if bodyStart < 0 {
			continue
		}
		bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
		if bodyEnd < 0 {
			continue
		}
		bodyDepth := depths[bodyStart] + 1
		out = append(out, methodsInBody(tokens, depths, bodyStart, bodyEnd, bodyDepth, className)...)
		i = bodyEnd
	}
	return out
}

// methodsInBody scans the class body for `name(...) { … }` at body-depth.
func methodsInBody(tokens []Token, depths []int, start, end, bodyDepth int, className string) []models.Function {
	var out []models.Function
	for i := start + 1; i < end; i++ {
		if depths[i] != bodyDepth {
			continue
		}
		// Skip modifiers: public, private, protected, static, async, readonly, abstract.
		j := skipMethodModifiers(tokens, i)
		if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokIdent {
			continue
		}
		// `name(`
		if j+1 >= len(tokens) || tokens[j+1].Kind != TokOpenParen {
			continue
		}
		// Skip the parameter list and any return-type annotation, look for `{`.
		closeParen := matchClosingParen(tokens, j+1)
		if closeParen < 0 {
			continue
		}
		bodyOpen := findNextOpenBrace(tokens, closeParen+1)
		if bodyOpen < 0 || bodyOpen >= end {
			continue
		}
		bodyClose := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyOpen)
		if bodyClose < 0 {
			continue
		}
		methodName := tokens[j].Text
		out = append(out, models.Function{
			Name:      methodName,
			Receiver:  className,
			Qualified: className + "." + methodName,
			Line:      tokens[i].Line,
			EndLine:   tokens[bodyClose].Line,
			Signature: renderTSSignature(tokens, j, bodyOpen),
		})
		i = bodyClose
	}
	return out
}

func skipClassModifiers(tokens []Token, i int) int {
	j := i
	for j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword {
		switch tokens[j].Text {
		case "export", "default", "abstract", "declare":
			j++
		default:
			return j
		}
	}
	return j
}

func skipMethodModifiers(tokens []Token, i int) int {
	j := i
	for j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword {
		switch tokens[j].Text {
		case "public", "private", "protected", "static", "async", "readonly", "abstract":
			j++
		default:
			return j
		}
	}
	return j
}

// readBracedDecl reads `class|interface|enum Name … { … }` starting at headerIdx
// (= the `class`/`interface`/`enum` keyword token index). Returns Class and the
// index of the closing brace.
func readBracedDecl(tokens []Token, formStart, headerIdx int, kind string) (models.Class, int, bool) {
	nameIdx := headerIdx + 1
	if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Class{}, headerIdx, false
	}
	bodyStart := findNextOpenBrace(tokens, nameIdx+1)
	if bodyStart < 0 {
		return models.Class{}, headerIdx, false
	}
	bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
	if bodyEnd < 0 {
		return models.Class{}, headerIdx, false
	}
	return models.Class{
		Name:      tokens[nameIdx].Text,
		Qualified: tokens[nameIdx].Text,
		Kind:      kind,
		Line:      tokens[formStart].Line,
		EndLine:   tokens[bodyEnd].Line,
	}, bodyEnd, true
}

// readTypeAlias reads `type Name = …;`. End-line is the semicolon line, or
// the line of the last non-blank token before the semicolon if there isn't one.
func readTypeAlias(tokens []Token, formStart, headerIdx int) (models.Class, int, bool) {
	nameIdx := headerIdx + 1
	if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Class{}, headerIdx, false
	}
	// Scan to the next semicolon at the same depth.
	endIdx := nameIdx
	for k := nameIdx + 1; k < len(tokens); k++ {
		if tokens[k].Kind == TokSemi {
			endIdx = k
			break
		}
		endIdx = k
	}
	return models.Class{
		Name:      tokens[nameIdx].Text,
		Qualified: tokens[nameIdx].Text,
		Kind:      "alias",
		Line:      tokens[formStart].Line,
		EndLine:   tokens[endIdx].Line,
	}, endIdx, true
}

// matchClosingParen returns the close-paren index that balances openIdx.
func matchClosingParen(tokens []Token, openIdx int) int {
	depth := 0
	for j := openIdx; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenParen {
			depth++
		} else if tokens[j].Kind == TokCloseParen {
			depth--
			if depth == 0 {
				return j
			}
		}
	}
	return -1
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests to verify they pass**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/typescript/ -run "TestParseClasses|TestParseMethods" -v
```
Expected: PASS for all three.

- [ ] **Step 6: Wire classes + methods into `Annotate`**

```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   languageForPath(path),
		Functions:  parseFunctions(source),
		Classes:    parseClasses(source),
		Imports:    parseImports(source),
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	md.Functions = append(md.Functions, parseMethods(source)...)
	if len(source) == 0 {
		md.Functions = []models.Function{}
		md.Classes = []models.Class{}
		md.Imports = []models.Import{}
		return md, nil
	}
	return md, nil
}
```

```bash
Class methods land as Function records with Receiver=ClassName and
Qualified='Class.Method' (matches the Go annotator's method shape).
Modifier keywords (export, default, abstract, declare for classes;
public/private/protected/static/async/readonly/abstract for methods) are
skipped before the declaration token. Type aliases use semicolon for
```
