## Task 10: JSX / TSX considerations

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/jsx.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/jsx_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/jsx.tsx.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/scanner.go` (add JSX-context awareness)
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go` (pass jsxEnabled to scanner)

The classic ambiguity: in `.tsx` files, `<Foo>` can mean either a TypeScript type-argument list (`identity<Foo>(x)`) or a JSX opening tag (`<Foo>content</Foo>`). The Babel parser disambiguates by context. For our hand-rolled scanner we use a simpler heuristic:

**JSX-context heuristic (only applied in .tsx/.jsx files):**

A `<` token is JSX-context iff:
1. The previous non-whitespace token is one of `=`, `(`, `,`, `{`, `}`, `=>`, `return`, `?`, `:`, `&&`, `||`, or BOF (i.e. we're in expression position, not after an identifier or `>`).
2. The character immediately following `<` is a letter or `/` (closing tag) — so `<foo>`, `<Foo>`, `<Foo/>`, `<>` (fragment) all qualify, but `< 1` (comparison) does not.

When the heuristic flags a `<`, we skip ahead to the matching JSX close — either `/>` for self-closing, or the matching `</Foo>`. JSX body content is discarded for annotation purposes (no symbols come from it).

Positive cases (must be JSX):
- `return <Foo />;`
- `const el = <Bar>{x}</Bar>;`
- `items.map((it) => <Item key={it.id} />)`
- `const wrapper = (<><Foo /><Bar /></>);` (fragments)

Negative cases (must NOT be JSX — must remain as generic / comparison):
- `identity<Foo>(x)` — generic call (preceded by ident `identity`).
- `if (a < b) { … }` — less-than comparison (followed by lowercase or non-alpha after spaces).
- `arr.map<number>((x) => x)` — generic method call.

For M2 we accept the heuristic's known limitation: a function call like `f<Foo>()` where `f` is a previously-emitted ident is correctly treated as a generic, but a fresh-line `<Foo>()` is a JSX self-closing element. Anyone writing the latter outside a JSX expression context is being unusual; the compat harness will surface it if real-world projects break.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/jsx.tsx.txt`:
```
import React from 'react';

interface Props {
    name: string;
}

// JSX-returning function — body must not confuse the scanner.
function Greeting(props: Props) {
    return <div className="hello">Hello {props.name}!</div>;
}

// Self-closing tag.
function Spinner() {
    return <Spinner />;
}

// Fragment.
function Fragment() {
    return <><Greeting name="a" /><Greeting name="b" /></>;
}

// Generic — NOT JSX.
function identity<T>(x: T): T {
    return x;
}

// Generic call — NOT JSX.
const wrapped = identity<string>("hi");

// Mapped children — JSX with an embedded expression.
function List({ items }: { items: string[] }) {
    return <ul>{items.map((it) => <li key={it}>{it}</li>)}</ul>;
}

class Counter {
    render(): JSX.Element {
        return <button onClick={() => this.tick()}>+1</button>;
    }
    tick(): void {}
}
```

```go
package typescript

import (

func TestAnnotate_TSX_FunctionsDetected(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "jsx.tsx.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("jsx.tsx", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	}
	for _, want := range []string{"Greeting", "Spinner", "Fragment", "identity", "List"} {
		require.True(t, names[want], "expected function %q", want)
	}
}

func TestAnnotate_TSX_ClassesDetected(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "jsx.tsx.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("jsx.tsx", src)

	names := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, c := range md.Classes {

func TestAnnotate_TSX_MethodsDetected(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "jsx.tsx.txt")

	methods := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {

	}
	require.True(t, methods["Counter.render"])
	require.True(t, methods["Counter.tick"])
}

func TestAnnotate_TSX_LineNumbersStable(t *testing.T) {
	// JSX should not eat into the next declaration's line range.
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "jsx.tsx.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("jsx.tsx", src)
	byName := indexFuncsByName(md.Functions)
	// identity is a small function — end-line within 3 of start.
	require.LessOrEqual(t, byName["identity"].EndLine-byName["identity"].Line, 3)
}

func TestSkipJSXElement_SelfClosing(t *testing.T) {
	// Standalone helper test — give it `<Foo />` and confirm we skip to past `/>`.
	tokens := Scan([]byte(`return <Foo />;`))
	// First `<` is the JSX `<`; skipJSXElement should return the index past `/>`.
	leftIdx := -1
	for i, t := range tokens {
		if t.Kind == TokOpenAngle && t.Text == "<" {
			leftIdx = i
			break
		}
	}
	require.GreaterOrEqual(t, leftIdx, 0)
	end := skipJSXElement(tokens, leftIdx)
	require.Greater(t, end, leftIdx)
}

func TestSkipJSXElement_PairedTag(t *testing.T) {
	tokens := Scan([]byte(`return <Foo><Bar/></Foo>;`))
	leftIdx := -1
	for i, t := range tokens {
		if t.Kind == TokOpenAngle && t.Text == "<" {
			leftIdx = i
			break
		}
	}
	require.GreaterOrEqual(t, leftIdx, 0)
	end := skipJSXElement(tokens, leftIdx)
	// End should be the last token (closing > of </Foo>).
	require.Equal(t, len(tokens)-2, end) // -2 because the trailing ';' is after.
}
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Implement JSX skipping**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/jsx.go`:
```go
package typescript

// isJSXContext returns true when the `<` at tokens[leftIdx] should be treated
// as a JSX opening tag rather than a less-than or generic. Heuristic:
//
//   1. The previous non-skippable token must be in expression position:
//        =  (  ,  {  }  =>  return  ?  :  &&  ||  !  ;  BOF
//   2. The character or token after `<` must look like a tag (an ident
//      starting with a letter, or `/` for closing tag, or `>` for fragment).
//
// This is conservative — false negatives (real JSX treated as comparison)
// degrade structural annotation gracefully; false positives (comparison
// treated as JSX) eat tokens and break parsing.
func isJSXContext(tokens []Token, leftIdx int) bool {
	if leftIdx == 0 {
		return jsxTagFollows(tokens, leftIdx)
	}
	prev := tokens[leftIdx-1]
	switch prev.Kind {
	case TokIdent, TokNumber, TokString, TokCloseParen, TokCloseBracket:
		// Definitely an expression value preceding — treat as comparison/generic.
		return false
	case TokCloseAngle:
		// `>` previously — most likely a generic close. Not JSX.
		return false
	}
	if prev.Kind == TokKeyword {
		switch prev.Text {
		case "return", "yield", "throw", "typeof", "instanceof", "of", "in", "await", "new", "void", "delete", "as":
			return jsxTagFollows(tokens, leftIdx)
		}
		return false
	}
	if prev.Kind == TokArrow || prev.Kind == TokComma || prev.Kind == TokSemi || prev.Kind == TokColon ||
		prev.Kind == TokOpenParen || prev.Kind == TokOpenBrace || prev.Kind == TokOpenBracket {
		return jsxTagFollows(tokens, leftIdx)
	}
	if prev.Kind == TokPunct {
		switch prev.Text {
		case "=", "==", "===", "!=", "!==", "&&", "||", "?", "!", "+", "-", "*", "/", "%":
			return jsxTagFollows(tokens, leftIdx)
		}
	}
	if prev.Kind == TokCloseBrace {
		return jsxTagFollows(tokens, leftIdx)
	}
	return false
}

// jsxTagFollows checks whether the token at leftIdx+1 looks like the
// start of a JSX tag name. Accepts:
//   <Ident…>      — opening tag
//   </…>          — closing tag (TokPunct '/')
//   <>            — fragment
func jsxTagFollows(tokens []Token, leftIdx int) bool {
	if leftIdx+1 >= len(tokens) {
		return false
	}
	next := tokens[leftIdx+1]
	switch next.Kind {
	case TokIdent:
		return true
	case TokCloseAngle:
		return true // <> fragment
	case TokPunct:
		return next.Text == "/"
	}
	return false
}

// skipJSXElement consumes one JSX element starting at the `<` token at idx
// and returns the index of the matching close (`>` of `</Foo>`, or `>` of
// `<Foo />`). When parsing fails it returns idx (no advance) so the caller
// can fall back to default handling.
//
// Algorithm: track JSX depth. Each `<Ident` increments depth; each `</…>`
// decrements; each self-closing `/>` does both. Embedded expressions
// (`{ … }`) are scanned with normal brace matching so internal symbols are
// recoverable by the higher-level parsers.
func skipJSXElement(tokens []Token, idx int) int {
	depth := 0
	i := idx
	for i < len(tokens) {
		t := tokens[i]
		switch t.Kind {
		case TokOpenAngle:
			// `</`?
			if i+1 < len(tokens) && tokens[i+1].Kind == TokPunct && tokens[i+1].Text == "/" {
				// closing tag — find the matching `>` and decrement.
				depth--
				for j := i + 1; j < len(tokens); j++ {
					if tokens[j].Kind == TokCloseAngle {
						i = j
						break
					}
				}
				if depth <= 0 {
					return i
				}
			} else {
				depth++
			}
		case TokPunct:
			// self-closing? Look at preceding token for `/` followed by `>`.
			if t.Text == "/" && i+1 < len(tokens) && tokens[i+1].Kind == TokCloseAngle {
				depth--
				i++ // consume the `>` too.
				if depth <= 0 {
					return i
				}
			}
		case TokOpenBrace:
			// Embedded expression `{ … }` — skip to matching close brace.
			closeBrace := matchClosingBrace(tokens, i)
			if closeBrace >= 0 {
				i = closeBrace
			}
		}
		i++
	}
	return i - 1
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Integrate JSX skipping into functions and classes**

The cleanest integration is at the scanner-consumer level: when one of the parsers encounters a `<` token in JSX context, it skips to the matching close and resumes. For M2 we take a simpler approach — we **pre-process the token stream** for `.tsx`/`.jsx` files, removing tokens between a JSX `<` and its matching close. The pruned token stream then flows through `parseFunctions`/`parseClasses`/`parseMethods` unchanged.

Modify `Annotate` in `annotator.go`:
```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   languageForPath(path),
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}

	jsxEnabled := strings.HasSuffix(path, ".tsx") || strings.HasSuffix(path, ".jsx")
	scanSource := source
	if jsxEnabled {
		// JSX pre-processor: replace JSX-element ranges with whitespace so
		// the downstream parsers see balanced source without JSX content.
		scanSource = stripJSXRanges(source)
	}

	md.Imports = parseImports(scanSource)
	md.Functions = parseFunctions(scanSource)
	md.Classes = parseClasses(scanSource)
	md.Functions = append(md.Functions, parseMethods(scanSource)...)

	return md, nil
}

// stripJSXRanges scans source, finds JSX ranges (using the same context
// heuristic as isJSXContext), and replaces the bytes inside each JSX
// element with spaces (preserving newlines so line numbers don't shift).
// Embedded `{ … }` expressions inside JSX are KEPT — they may contain
// symbols (callbacks, etc.) we want to detect.
func stripJSXRanges(source []byte) []byte {
	tokens := Scan(source)
	type rng struct{ start, end int } // byte offsets
	var ranges []rng
	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		if tokens[i].Kind != TokOpenAngle {
			continue
		}
		if !isJSXContext(tokens, i) {
			continue
		}
		closeIdx := skipJSXElement(tokens, i)
		if closeIdx <= i {
			continue
		}
		startByte := tokens[i].Offset
		endByte := tokens[closeIdx].Offset + len(tokens[closeIdx].Text)
		ranges = append(ranges, rng{startByte, endByte})
		i = closeIdx
	}
	if len(ranges) == 0 {
		return source
	}
	out := make([]byte, len(source))
	copy(out, source)
	for _, r := range ranges {
		for k := r.start; k < r.end && k < len(out); k++ {
			if out[k] != '\n' {
				out[k] = ' '
			}
		}
	}
	return out
}
```

Expected: PASS for every test in the package. The TSX tests should now find Greeting/Spinner/etc. and ignore JSX bodies.

```bash
git commit -m "feat(annotator/typescript): JSX/TSX pre-processor for .tsx/.jsx

isJSXContext heuristic: '<' is JSX iff preceded by an expression-position
token and followed by ident/'/'/'>'. stripJSXRanges replaces JSX-element
bytes with spaces (preserving newlines so line numbers stay stable) before
the standard parsers run. Embedded {expr} blocks inside JSX are kept so
callback symbols are still detected. Generic forms ('identity<T>',
'identity<string>(x)') correctly stay outside the JSX path."
```

## Task 11: Call edges

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/calls.go`, `internal/annotator/typescript/calls_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/calls.ts.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go`

Call edges populate `DepGraph` for the nav tools later in Phase 5. We extract one edge per call expression in each function body. The `From` field is the enclosing function/method's `Qualified` name; the `To` field is the callee as written:

- `helper()` → `To = "helper"`
- `obj.method()` → `To = "obj.method"`
- `pkg.fn()` → `To = "pkg.fn"`
- `this.tick()` → `To = "this.tick"` (the dep-graph resolver in Task 28 normalises `this.X` to the receiver class name based on the From symbol)

Edges from non-identifier receivers (`(await x).foo()`, `arr[0].bar()`) are skipped — same lossy posture as the Go annotator.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/calls.ts.txt`:
```
function helper() { return 1; }
function outer() {
    helper();
    console.log("x");
    Math.max(1, 2);
    return helper();
}

class Service {
    fetch(): number {
        return this.parse(this.load());
    }
    parse(raw: number): number { return raw + 1; }
    load(): number { return 7; }
}

const arrow = () => helper();
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/calls_test.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"
)

func TestParseCalls_OuterFunction(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "calls.ts.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("calls.ts", src)

	edges := edgesFrom(md.Calls, "outer")
	tos := toList(edges)
	require.Contains(t, tos, "helper")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "console.log")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "Math.max")
}

func TestParseCalls_MethodCallsResolveThis(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "calls.ts.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("calls.ts", src)

	edges := edgesFrom(md.Calls, "Service.fetch")
	tos := toList(edges)
	require.Contains(t, tos, "this.parse")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "this.load")
}

func TestParseCalls_ArrowFunction(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "calls.ts.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("calls.ts", src)

	edges := edgesFrom(md.Calls, "arrow")
	require.Equal(t, 1, len(edges))
	require.Equal(t, "helper", edges[0].To)
}

func edgesFrom(edges []models.SymbolRef, from string) []models.SymbolRef {
	var out []models.SymbolRef
	for _, e := range edges {
		if e.From == from {
			out = append(out, e)
		}
	}
	return out
}

func toList(edges []models.SymbolRef) []string {
	out := make([]string, len(edges))
	for i, e := range edges {
		out[i] = e.To
	}
	return out
}
```

Add to the file's imports:
```go

	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Implement the call-edge extractor**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/calls.go`:
```go
package typescript

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseCalls walks the token stream and emits one SymbolRef per CallExpr
// found inside any of the supplied functions. The function list must be
// the post-parseFunctions+parseMethods result so we have accurate Line/EndLine
// ranges to scope each call to its containing function.
//
// To-field shapes:
//   helper()           -> To = "helper"
//   pkg.fn()           -> To = "pkg.fn"
//   this.method()      -> To = "this.method"   (graph resolver normalises later)
//
// Non-identifier callees ((await x).foo(), arr[0].bar(), getThing()()) are
// skipped — same lossy posture as Go.
func parseCalls(source []byte, funcs []models.Function) []models.SymbolRef {
	tokens := Scan(source)
	if len(tokens) == 0 || len(funcs) == 0 {
		return nil
	}
	// Index call sites by line so we can attribute them to a function.
	var out []models.SymbolRef
	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		// Must look like `<ident>(` or `<ident>.<ident>(` or `this.<ident>(`.
		if tokens[i].Kind != TokIdent && !(tokens[i].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[i].Text == "this") {
			continue
		}
		// Build the call target.
		var target string
		end := i
		if tokens[i].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[i].Text == "this" {
			if i+2 < len(tokens) && tokens[i+1].Kind == TokPunct && tokens[i+1].Text == "." && tokens[i+2].Kind == TokIdent {
				target = "this." + tokens[i+2].Text
				end = i + 2
			} else {
				continue
			}
		} else {
			target = tokens[i].Text
			if i+2 < len(tokens) && tokens[i+1].Kind == TokPunct && tokens[i+1].Text == "." && tokens[i+2].Kind == TokIdent {
				target = target + "." + tokens[i+2].Text
				end = i + 2
			}
		}
		// After target, must be `(`.
		if end+1 >= len(tokens) || tokens[end+1].Kind != TokOpenParen {
			continue
		}
		// Find enclosing function.
		callLine := tokens[i].Line
		fromName := enclosingFunction(funcs, callLine)
		if fromName == "" {
			continue
		}
		out = append(out, models.SymbolRef{
			From: fromName,
			To:   target,
			Line: callLine,
		})
		i = end
	}
	return out
}

// enclosingFunction returns the Qualified name of the innermost function
// whose Line..EndLine range contains line. Nested functions are resolved by
// preferring the function with the smallest range.
func enclosingFunction(funcs []models.Function, line int) string {
	best := ""
	bestRange := 1 << 30
	for _, f := range funcs {
		if line < f.Line || line > f.EndLine {
			continue
		}
		r := f.EndLine - f.Line
		if r < bestRange {
			bestRange = r
			best = f.Qualified
		}
	}
	return best
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Wire calls into `Annotate`**

```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   languageForPath(path),
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}

	jsxEnabled := strings.HasSuffix(path, ".tsx") || strings.HasSuffix(path, ".jsx")
	scanSource := source
	if jsxEnabled {
		scanSource = stripJSXRanges(source)
	}

	md.Imports = parseImports(scanSource)
	md.Functions = parseFunctions(scanSource)
	md.Classes = parseClasses(scanSource)
	md.Functions = append(md.Functions, parseMethods(scanSource)...)
	md.Calls = parseCalls(scanSource, md.Functions)

	return md, nil
}
```

- [ ] **Step 6: Run the tests**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/typescript/ -v
```
Expected: PASS for every test in the package.

- [ ] **Step 7: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/typescript/calls.go internal/annotator/typescript/calls_test.go internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/calls.ts.txt internal/annotator/typescript/annotator.go
git commit -m "feat(annotator/typescript): extract call-edge graph

One SymbolRef per CallExpr. Targets: bare ident ('helper'), member
('pkg.fn'), this-method ('this.method' — graph resolver normalises
later). Non-identifier callees skipped — lossy by design, matches Go
annotator's posture. Enclosing-function attribution uses smallest-range
function whose Line..EndLine contains the call site, so nested functions
attribute calls correctly."
```

## Task 12: TS end-to-end test + wire into binaries

**Files:**
- Modify: `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator_test.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/realistic.tsx.txt`
- Modify: `cmd/token-savior/main.go`, `cmd/ts-compat/main.go`

Adds a realistic ~80-line TSX fixture (modelled on a Next.js page) and exercises every M2 TS feature end-to-end. Also blank-imports the typescript package from both binaries so the annotator is live.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the realistic fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/typescript/testdata/realistic.tsx.txt`:
```
import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react';
import type { User } from './types';
import { fetchUser } from './api';

interface ProfileProps {
    userId: string;
    onError: (e: Error) => void;
}

type AvatarSize = 'sm' | 'md' | 'lg';

enum Status {
    LOADING,
    READY,
    ERROR,
}

const SIZES: Record<AvatarSize, number> = { sm: 32, md: 48, lg: 64 };

function pixelSize(size: AvatarSize): number {
    return SIZES[size];
}

const formatName = (u: User) => `${u.first} ${u.last}`;

export default function Profile({ userId, onError }: ProfileProps) {
    const [user, setUser] = useState<User | null>(null);
    const [status, setStatus] = useState<Status>(Status.LOADING);

    useEffect(() => {
        fetchUser(userId)
            .then((u) => {
                setUser(u);
                setStatus(Status.READY);
            })
            .catch((err) => {
                onError(err);
                setStatus(Status.ERROR);
            });
    }, [userId, onError]);

    if (status === Status.LOADING) {
        return <div className="loading">Loading…</div>;
    }
    if (!user) {
        return <div className="error">No user.</div>;
    }
    return (
        <div className="profile">
            <img src={user.avatarUrl} width={pixelSize('md')} alt="" />
            <h1>{formatName(user)}</h1>
        </div>
    );
}

export class AvatarCache {
    private cache = new Map<string, string>();
    get(key: string): string | undefined { return this.cache.get(key); }
    set(key: string, url: string): void { this.cache.set(key, url); }
    clear(): void { this.cache.clear(); }
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the end-to-end test**

Append to `internal/annotator/typescript/annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestAnnotate_RealisticTSX_E2E(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "realistic.tsx.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("realistic.tsx", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	// Imports: react, ./types, ./api.
	importPaths := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, im := range md.Imports {
		importPaths[im.Path] = true
	}
	require.True(t, importPaths["react"])
	require.True(t, importPaths["./types"])
	require.True(t, importPaths["./api"])

	// Top-level functions: pixelSize, formatName, Profile.
	fnames := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {
		fnames[f.Name] = true
	}
	require.True(t, fnames["pixelSize"])
	require.True(t, fnames["formatName"])
	require.True(t, fnames["Profile"])

	// Class methods: AvatarCache.get/set/clear.
	require.True(t, fnames["get"])
	require.True(t, fnames["set"])
	require.True(t, fnames["clear"])

	// Classes/interfaces/types/enums.
	cnames := make(map[string]string)
	for _, c := range md.Classes {
		cnames[c.Name] = c.Kind
	}
	require.Equal(t, "interface", cnames["ProfileProps"])
	require.Equal(t, "alias", cnames["AvatarSize"])
	require.Equal(t, "enum", cnames["Status"])
	require.Equal(t, "class", cnames["AvatarCache"])

	// Calls: Profile should call useState, useEffect, fetchUser, pixelSize, formatName.
	var profileCalls []string
	for _, e := range md.Calls {
		if e.From == "Profile" {
			profileCalls = append(profileCalls, e.To)
		}
	}
	require.Contains(t, profileCalls, "useState")
	require.Contains(t, profileCalls, "useEffect")
	require.Contains(t, profileCalls, "fetchUser")
}
```

## Phase 3: Rust annotator

Smaller and more uniform than TS. Rust syntax is regular at the item level — `fn`, `struct`, `enum`, `trait`, `impl Foo for Bar`, `mod`, `use`, `macro_rules!` are all word-keyword-prefixed declarations. The tokenizer mirrors the TS scanner shape (brace/paren/string depth, line comments, block comments, raw strings, attributes), with two Rust-specific concerns:

- **Raw strings:** `r"…"`, `r#"…"#`, `r##"…"##` with N `#`s on each side. The N is variable; the closer must match.
- **Lifetimes vs char literals:** `'a` is a lifetime; `'a'` is a char. Heuristic: if the char after the second `'` is an identifier char, treat as char; else treat as lifetime.

Macros (`macro_rules!`) get a name-only annotation; the body isn't expanded.

Python's annotator: `src/token_savior/rust_annotator.py` (~740 LoC). Grep `_USE_RE`, `_FN_RE`, `_STRUCT_RE`, `_TRAIT_RE`, `_IMPL_RE`, `_MACRO_RULES_RE` for shape reference.

## Task 13: Rust annotator skeleton + dispatch

- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/empty.rs.txt`, `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/comments_only.rs.txt`

- [ ] **Step 4: Create the skeleton**

```go
// Package rust annotates Rust source (.rs) using a hand-rolled tokenizer.
// Scope: fn, struct, enum, trait, impl, mod, use, macro_rules!. Macros are
// detected by name only; bodies are not expanded.
package rust

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

func init() {
	annotator.Register("rust", New())
}

// Annotator is the Rust annotator. Safe for concurrent use.
type Annotator struct{}

// New returns a Rust annotator.
func New() *Annotator { return &Annotator{} }

// Annotate parses Rust source and emits structural metadata.
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "rust",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}
	// Task 14-17 fill these in.
	return md, nil
}
```

## Task 14: Rust scanner

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/scanner.go`, `internal/annotator/rust/scanner_test.go`

The Rust scanner is structurally simpler than TS: no JSX, no template literals, no regex literal syntax. The two Rust-specific complications are raw strings and lifetime-vs-char.

- [ ] **Step 1: Write the failing scanner test**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/scanner_test.go`:
```go
package rust

import (
	"testing"

	"github.com/stretchr/testify/require"
)

func TestScan_Empty(t *testing.T) {
	require.Empty(t, Scan(nil))
}

func TestScan_KeywordsAndIdents(t *testing.T) {
	toks := Scan([]byte("fn foo(x: i32) -> i32 { x }"))
	kinds := tokenKinds(toks)
	require.Contains(t, kinds, TokKeyword)
	require.Contains(t, kinds, TokIdent)
}

func TestScan_LineComment(t *testing.T) {
	toks := Scan([]byte("fn a() {}\n// comment\nfn b() {}"))
	require.Equal(t, 2, countTokens(toks, TokKeyword, "fn"))
}

func TestScan_BlockComment(t *testing.T) {
	toks := Scan([]byte("/* multi\nline */\nfn a() {}"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(toks, TokKeyword, "fn"))
}

func TestScan_NestedBlockComment(t *testing.T) {
	// Rust supports nested block comments.
	toks := Scan([]byte("/* outer /* inner */ still outer */\nfn a() {}"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(toks, TokKeyword, "fn"))
}

func TestScan_StringLiteral(t *testing.T) {
	toks := Scan([]byte(`fn a() { let s = "with {brace}"; }`))
	// Brace inside string should NOT register as TokOpenBrace.
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(toks, TokOpenBrace), "outer fn body brace only")
}

func TestScan_RawString(t *testing.T) {
	toks := Scan([]byte(`fn a() { let s = r#"with "quotes" and {brace}"#; }`))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(toks, TokOpenBrace))
}

func TestScan_RawStringWithMultipleHashes(t *testing.T) {
	toks := Scan([]byte(`fn a() { let s = r##"contains "# but not "##; }`))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokenKind(toks, TokOpenBrace))
}

func TestScan_CharVsLifetime(t *testing.T) {
	// 'a' is a char; 'a is a lifetime.
	toks := Scan([]byte("fn f<'a>(x: &'a str) -> char { 'z' }"))
	// We should see both the lifetime '\'a' tokens and the char '\'z\''.
	idents := 0
	for _, t := range toks {
		if t.Kind == TokIdent {
			idents++
		}
	}
	require.Greater(t, idents, 0)
}

func TestScan_Attributes(t *testing.T) {
	// Attributes #[derive(Debug)] should not break parsing.
	toks := Scan([]byte("#[derive(Debug)]\nstruct Foo;"))
	require.Equal(t, 1, countTokens(toks, TokKeyword, "struct"))
}

func tokenKinds(toks []Token) []TokenKind {
	out := make([]TokenKind, len(toks))
	for i, t := range toks {
		out[i] = t.Kind
	}
	return out
}

func countTokens(toks []Token, kind TokenKind, text string) int {
	n := 0
	for _, t := range toks {
		if t.Kind == kind && t.Text == text {
			n++
		}
	}
	return n
}

func countTokenKind(toks []Token, kind TokenKind) int {
	n := 0
	for _, t := range toks {
		if t.Kind == kind {
			n++
		}
	}
	return n
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Run the test to verify it fails**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/rust/ -run TestScan -v
```
Expected: FAIL — `undefined: Scan, Token, TokenKind`.

- [ ] **Step 3: Implement the Rust scanner**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/scanner.go`:
```go
package rust

// TokenKind enumerates scanner output kinds.
type TokenKind int

const (
	TokInvalid TokenKind = iota
	TokKeyword
	TokIdent
	TokNumber
	TokString
	TokChar
	TokLifetime
	TokPunct
	TokOpenBrace
	TokCloseBrace
	TokOpenParen
	TokCloseParen
	TokOpenBracket
	TokCloseBracket
	TokOpenAngle
	TokCloseAngle
	TokSemi
	TokComma
	TokColon
	TokDoubleColon // ::
	TokArrow       // ->
	TokFatArrow    // =>
	TokHash        // #
	TokBang        // ! (also macro indicator)
)

type Token struct {
	Kind   TokenKind
	Text   string
	Offset int
	Line   int
	Column int
}

var keywords = map[string]bool{
	"as": true, "async": true, "await": true, "break": true, "const": true,
	"continue": true, "crate": true, "dyn": true, "else": true, "enum": true,
	"extern": true, "false": true, "fn": true, "for": true, "if": true,
	"impl": true, "in": true, "let": true, "loop": true, "match": true,
	"mod": true, "move": true, "mut": true, "pub": true, "ref": true,
	"return": true, "self": true, "Self": true, "static": true, "struct": true,
	"super": true, "trait": true, "true": true, "type": true, "unsafe": true,
	"use": true, "where": true, "while": true,
}

// Scan tokenises Rust source.
func Scan(source []byte) []Token {
	s := &scanner{src: source, line: 1, col: 1}
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		s.next()
	}
	return s.tokens
}

type scanner struct {
	src    []byte
	offset int
	line   int
	col    int
	tokens []Token
}

func (s *scanner) emit(kind TokenKind, text string, off, line, col int) {
	s.tokens = append(s.tokens, Token{Kind: kind, Text: text, Offset: off, Line: line, Column: col})
}

func (s *scanner) peek() byte {
	if s.offset >= len(s.src) {
		return 0
	}
	return s.src[s.offset]
}

func (s *scanner) peekAt(n int) byte {
	if s.offset+n >= len(s.src) {
		return 0
	}
	return s.src[s.offset+n]
}

func (s *scanner) advance() byte {
	if s.offset >= len(s.src) {
		return 0
	}
	b := s.src[s.offset]
	s.offset++
	if b == '\n' {
		s.line++
		s.col = 1
	} else {
		s.col++
	}
	return b
}

func (s *scanner) next() {
	c := s.peek()
	switch {
	case c == ' ' || c == '\t' || c == '\n' || c == '\r':
		s.advance()
	case c == '/' && s.peekAt(1) == '/':
		s.skipLineComment()
	case c == '/' && s.peekAt(1) == '*':
		s.skipBlockComment()
	case c == '"':
		s.scanString()
	case c == 'r' && (s.peekAt(1) == '"' || s.peekAt(1) == '#'):
		// Raw string (must also check that this isn't an ident starting with 'r').
		if s.peekAt(1) == '"' || (s.peekAt(1) == '#' && (s.peekAt(2) == '"' || s.peekAt(2) == '#')) {
			s.scanRawString()
			return
		}
		s.scanIdentOrKeyword()
	case c == '\'':
		s.scanCharOrLifetime()
	case c == 'b' && s.peekAt(1) == '"':
		// Byte string b"…"
		s.advance()
		s.scanString()
	case isIdentStart(c):
		s.scanIdentOrKeyword()
	case c >= '0' && c <= '9':
		s.scanNumber()
	default:
		s.scanPunct()
	}
}

func (s *scanner) skipLineComment() {
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && s.src[s.offset] != '\n' {
		s.advance()
	}
}

// skipBlockComment handles nested /* … */.
func (s *scanner) skipBlockComment() {
	s.advance() // /
	s.advance() // *
	depth := 1
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && depth > 0 {
		if s.peek() == '/' && s.peekAt(1) == '*' {
			s.advance()
			s.advance()
			depth++
			continue
		}
		if s.peek() == '*' && s.peekAt(1) == '/' {
			s.advance()
			s.advance()
			depth--
			continue
		}
		s.advance()
	}
}

func (s *scanner) scanString() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	s.advance() // opening "
	var buf []byte
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.peek()
		if c == '\\' {
			s.advance()
			if s.offset < len(s.src) {
				buf = append(buf, s.advance())
			}
			continue
		}
		if c == '"' {
			s.advance()
			break
		}
		buf = append(buf, s.advance())
	}
	s.emit(TokString, string(buf), off, line, col)
}

// scanRawString handles r"…", r#"…"#, r##"…"##, …
func (s *scanner) scanRawString() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	s.advance() // r
	hashes := 0
	for s.peek() == '#' {
		hashes++
		s.advance()
	}
	if s.peek() != '"' {
		// Not actually a raw string; treat as ident "r" plus rest.
		s.emit(TokIdent, "r", off, line, col)
		return
	}
	s.advance() // "
	var buf []byte
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		if s.peek() == '"' {
			// Check that the next `hashes` chars are all '#'.
			ok := true
			for k := 0; k < hashes; k++ {
				if s.peekAt(1+k) != '#' {
					ok = false
					break
				}
			}
			if ok {
				s.advance() // closing "
				for k := 0; k < hashes; k++ {
					s.advance() // #
				}
				break
			}
		}
		buf = append(buf, s.advance())
	}
	s.emit(TokString, string(buf), off, line, col)
}

// scanCharOrLifetime: '<ident_start>(') → char; otherwise lifetime.
func (s *scanner) scanCharOrLifetime() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	s.advance() // opening '
	// Is the next char a starter and the one after is a closing '?
	if isIdentStart(s.peek()) {
		// Could be lifetime ('a) or char ('a').
		// Look two ahead — if there's a closing quote, it's a char.
		// Otherwise it's a lifetime.
		if s.peekAt(1) == '\'' {
			s.advance() // ident char
			s.advance() // closing '
			s.emit(TokChar, "", off, line, col)
			return
		}
		// Lifetime: consume the ident.
		var buf []byte
		for isIdentPart(s.peek()) {
			buf = append(buf, s.advance())
		}
		s.emit(TokLifetime, "'"+string(buf), off, line, col)
		return
	}
	// Char literal with escape or non-ident: 'a', '\n', '\u{…}', etc.
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && s.peek() != '\'' {
		if s.peek() == '\\' {
			s.advance()
			if s.offset < len(s.src) {
				s.advance()
			}
			continue
		}
		s.advance()
	}
	if s.peek() == '\'' {
		s.advance()
	}
	s.emit(TokChar, "", off, line, col)
}

func (s *scanner) scanIdentOrKeyword() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	start := s.offset
	for s.offset < len(s.src) && isIdentPart(s.src[s.offset]) {
		s.advance()
	}
	text := string(s.src[start:s.offset])
	if keywords[text] {
		s.emit(TokKeyword, text, off, line, col)
	} else {
		s.emit(TokIdent, text, off, line, col)
	}
}

func (s *scanner) scanNumber() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	start := s.offset
	for s.offset < len(s.src) {
		c := s.src[s.offset]
		if (c >= '0' && c <= '9') || c == '.' || c == '_' || c == 'x' || c == 'X' || c == 'e' || c == 'E' ||
			(c >= 'a' && c <= 'f') || (c >= 'A' && c <= 'F') || c == 'i' || c == 'u' || c == 'f' {
			s.advance()
		} else {
			break
		}
	}
	s.emit(TokNumber, string(s.src[start:s.offset]), off, line, col)
}

func (s *scanner) scanPunct() {
	off, line, col := s.offset, s.line, s.col
	c := s.advance()
	switch c {
	case '{':
		s.emit(TokOpenBrace, "{", off, line, col)
	case '}':
		s.emit(TokCloseBrace, "}", off, line, col)
	case '(':
		s.emit(TokOpenParen, "(", off, line, col)
	case ')':
		s.emit(TokCloseParen, ")", off, line, col)
	case '[':
		s.emit(TokOpenBracket, "[", off, line, col)
	case ']':
		s.emit(TokCloseBracket, "]", off, line, col)
	case ';':
		s.emit(TokSemi, ";", off, line, col)
	case ',':
		s.emit(TokComma, ",", off, line, col)
	case ':':
		if s.peek() == ':' {
			s.advance()
			s.emit(TokDoubleColon, "::", off, line, col)
		} else {
			s.emit(TokColon, ":", off, line, col)
		}
	case '#':
		s.emit(TokHash, "#", off, line, col)
	case '!':
		s.emit(TokBang, "!", off, line, col)
	case '-':
		if s.peek() == '>' {
			s.advance()
			s.emit(TokArrow, "->", off, line, col)
		} else {
			s.emit(TokPunct, "-", off, line, col)
		}
	case '=':
		if s.peek() == '>' {
			s.advance()
			s.emit(TokFatArrow, "=>", off, line, col)
		} else {
			s.emit(TokPunct, "=", off, line, col)
		}
	case '<':
		s.emit(TokOpenAngle, "<", off, line, col)
	case '>':
		s.emit(TokCloseAngle, ">", off, line, col)
	default:
		s.emit(TokPunct, string(c), off, line, col)
	}
}

func isIdentStart(c byte) bool {
	return c == '_' || (c >= 'a' && c <= 'z') || (c >= 'A' && c <= 'Z')
}

func isIdentPart(c byte) bool {
	return isIdentStart(c) || (c >= '0' && c <= '9')
}
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Run the scanner tests**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/rust/ -run TestScan -v
```
Expected: PASS for every scanner test.

- [ ] **Step 5: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/rust/scanner.go internal/annotator/rust/scanner_test.go
git commit -m "feat(annotator/rust): byte-level scanner with raw strings + lifetimes

Handles line/block comments (with Rust's nested block-comment rule),
single-quoted strings with escape, raw strings (r\"…\", r#\"…\"#, …),
byte strings (b\"…\"), char vs lifetime disambiguation (look-ahead for
closing quote), attributes (#[…]), and the punctuation set Rust care
about (::, ->, =>, !, #)."
```

## Task 15: use / mod parsing

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/use.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/use.rs.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/rust/annotator.go`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/rust/annotator_test.go`

`use` statements yield `Import` entries. Multi-import forms (`use std::collections::{HashMap, HashSet};`) collapse into a single `Import` with the path as written (we don't explode per-name — same posture as TS).

`mod` declarations come in two forms:
- `mod foo;` — refers to `foo.rs` (or `foo/mod.rs`). Recorded as an Import with path `foo`.
- `mod foo { … }` — inline submodule definition. Recorded as a Class with kind `"alias"` (closest existing kind) so submodules appear in the symbol table.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/use.rs.txt`:
```
use std::collections::HashMap;
use std::collections::{HashSet, BTreeMap};
use crate::config::Settings;
use super::utils::*;
pub use crate::error::Error;
use std::io::{
    self,
    BufRead,
    Write,
};

mod parser;
mod inline_mod {
    pub fn hi() {}
}

extern crate serde;
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Append to `internal/annotator/rust/annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestParseUses_AllForms(t *testing.T) {

	md, err := New().Annotate("use.rs", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	paths := make([]string, 0, len(md.Imports))
	for _, im := range md.Imports {
		paths = append(paths, im.Path)
	}
	require.Contains(t, paths, "std::collections::HashMap")
	require.Contains(t, paths, "crate::config::Settings")
	require.Contains(t, paths, "super::utils::*")
	require.Contains(t, paths, "crate::error::Error")
	// File-mod ref.
	require.Contains(t, paths, "parser")
}

func TestParseMods_InlineModule(t *testing.T) {

	names := make(map[string]bool)

		names[c.Name] = true

}
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Implement use + mod parsing**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/use.go`:
```go
package rust

import (
	"strings"

	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseUses extracts `use` statements (and `pub use`) into Imports. Each
// use-clause is one Import; multi-imports (`use a::{b, c}`) collapse into
// a single Import with the raw path text.
func parseUses(tokens []Token) []models.Import {
	var out []models.Import
	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		if !isUseStart(tokens, i) {
			continue
		}
		// Skip optional `pub`.
		j := i
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[j].Text == "pub" {
			j++
		}
		if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokKeyword || tokens[j].Text != "use" {
			continue
		}
		// Collect tokens until a `;` at depth 0.
		var b strings.Builder
		depth := 0
		startLine := tokens[i].Line
		end := j
		for k := j + 1; k < len(tokens); k++ {
			t := tokens[k]
			if t.Kind == TokOpenBrace {
				depth++
			} else if t.Kind == TokCloseBrace {
				depth--
			}
			if t.Kind == TokSemi && depth == 0 {
				end = k
				break
			}
			if b.Len() > 0 {
				b.WriteByte(' ')
			}
			b.WriteString(t.Text)
		}
		path := strings.TrimSpace(b.String())
		path = collapseWhitespace(path)
		if path != "" {
			out = append(out, models.Import{Path: path, Line: startLine})
		}
		i = end
	}
	return out
}

// parseMods extracts `mod foo;` (file-mod refs → Imports) and `mod foo { … }`
// (inline modules → Classes).
func parseMods(tokens []Token) ([]models.Import, []models.Class) {
	var imps []models.Import
	var classes []models.Class
	depths := computeBraceDepths(tokens)
	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		if depths[i] > 0 {
			continue
		}
		j := i
		// Skip optional pub.
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[j].Text == "pub" {
			j++
		}
		if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokKeyword || tokens[j].Text != "mod" {
			continue
		}
		nameIdx := j + 1
		if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
			continue
		}
		name := tokens[nameIdx].Text
		// Followed by `;` (file mod) or `{` (inline).
		after := nameIdx + 1
		if after < len(tokens) && tokens[after].Kind == TokSemi {
			imps = append(imps, models.Import{Path: name, Line: tokens[i].Line})
			i = after
			continue
		}
		if after < len(tokens) && tokens[after].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			closeIdx := matchClosingBrace(tokens, after)
			endLine := tokens[after].Line
			if closeIdx >= 0 {
				endLine = tokens[closeIdx].Line
			}
			classes = append(classes, models.Class{
				Name:      name,
				Qualified: name,
				Kind:      "alias", // module → alias slot (no dedicated kind in models.Class)
				Line:      tokens[i].Line,
				EndLine:   endLine,
			})
			if closeIdx >= 0 {
				i = closeIdx
			} else {
				i = after
			}
			continue
		}
	}
	return imps, classes
}

// isUseStart returns true when tokens[i] is the start of a use/pub-use statement.
func isUseStart(tokens []Token, i int) bool {
	if tokens[i].Kind != TokKeyword {
		return false
	}
	if tokens[i].Text == "use" {
		return true
	}
	if tokens[i].Text == "pub" && i+1 < len(tokens) && tokens[i+1].Kind == TokKeyword && tokens[i+1].Text == "use" {
		return true
	}
	return false
}

// computeBraceDepths is a shared helper — same shape as the TS version.
func computeBraceDepths(tokens []Token) []int {
	out := make([]int, len(tokens))
	depth := 0
	for i, t := range tokens {
		out[i] = depth
		if t.Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			depth++
		} else if t.Kind == TokCloseBrace {
			depth--
		}
	}
	return out
}

// matchClosingBrace returns the close-brace index that balances openIdx.
func matchClosingBrace(tokens []Token, openIdx int) int {
	depth := 0
	for j := openIdx; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			depth++
		} else if tokens[j].Kind == TokCloseBrace {
			depth--
			if depth == 0 {
				return j
			}
		}
	}
	return -1
}

func collapseWhitespace(s string) string {
	var b strings.Builder
	inSpace := false
	for i := 0; i < len(s); i++ {
		c := s[i]
		if c == ' ' || c == '\t' {
			if !inSpace {
				b.WriteByte(' ')
				inSpace = true
			}
			continue
		}
		inSpace = false
		b.WriteByte(c)
	}
	return b.String()
}
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Wire into Annotate**

```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "rust",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}
	tokens := Scan(source)
	md.Imports = parseUses(tokens)
	modImps, modClasses := parseMods(tokens)
	md.Imports = append(md.Imports, modImps...)
	md.Classes = append(md.Classes, modClasses...)
	return md, nil
}
```

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/rust/ -v
```
Expected: PASS.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/rust/use.go internal/annotator/rust/testdata/use.rs.txt internal/annotator/rust/annotator.go internal/annotator/rust/annotator_test.go
git commit -m "feat(annotator/rust): parse use / pub-use / mod statements

One Import per use-clause (multi-imports collapse). 'mod foo;' is an
Import; 'mod foo { … }' is a Class (alias kind — closest fit in
models.Class without adding a 'module' kind). Brace-depth bookkeeping
shared via computeBraceDepths + matchClosingBrace helpers."
```

## Task 16: Items — fn / struct / enum / trait / impl / macro_rules

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/items.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/items.rs.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/rust/annotator.go`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/rust/annotator_test.go`

Item declarations:

| Source | Output |
|---|---|
| `fn foo(…) -> T { … }` | `Function{Name: "foo", Qualified: "foo"}` |
| `pub async fn bar() { … }` | same — modifiers stripped |
| `struct Point { x: f64, y: f64 }` | `Class{Name: "Point", Kind: "struct"}` |
| `enum Color { R, G, B }` | `Class{Name: "Color", Kind: "enum"}` |
| `trait Greeter { fn hello(&self); }` | `Class{Name: "Greeter", Kind: "interface"}` (mapped to "interface" in `models.Class`) |
| `impl Foo { fn x() {} }` | methods on Foo |
| `impl Trait for Type { fn y() {} }` | methods on Type |
| `macro_rules! my_macro { … }` | `Function{Name: "my_macro", Signature: "macro_rules!"}` |

Methods inside `impl` blocks get `Receiver` = type name and `Qualified` = `"Type.method"`. For `impl Trait for Type`, the trait name is **not** prepended — Python's annotator uses the receiver type, and the dep-graph cares about the implementing type, not the trait.

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/items.rs.txt`:
```
pub fn add(a: i32, b: i32) -> i32 {
    a + b
}

async fn fetch_user(id: u64) -> Result<User, Error> {
    Ok(User { id })
}

const fn pi() -> f64 { 3.14 }

pub struct Point {
    pub x: f64,
    pub y: f64,
}

pub struct Tuple(pub i32, pub i32);

pub struct Unit;

pub enum Color {
    Red,
    Green,
    Blue,
    Custom(u8, u8, u8),
    Hex { value: u32 },
}

pub trait Greeter {
    fn hello(&self) -> String;
    fn goodbye(&self) -> String {
        String::from("bye")
    }
}

impl Point {
    pub fn new(x: f64, y: f64) -> Self {
        Point { x, y }
    }
    pub fn distance(&self, other: &Point) -> f64 {
        ((self.x - other.x).powi(2) + (self.y - other.y).powi(2)).sqrt()
    }
}

impl Greeter for Point {
    fn hello(&self) -> String {
        format!("Hello from ({}, {})", self.x, self.y)
    }
}

macro_rules! shout {
    ($x:expr) => { format!("{}!", $x) };
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Append to `annotator_test.go`:

```go
func TestParseItems_Functions(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "items.rs.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("items.rs", src)

	names := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {
		names[f.Name] = true
	}
	require.True(t, names["add"])
	require.True(t, names["fetch_user"])
	require.True(t, names["pi"])
}

func TestParseItems_Types(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "items.rs.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("items.rs", src)

	byName := make(map[string]string)
	for _, c := range md.Classes {
		byName[c.Name] = c.Kind
	}
	require.Equal(t, "struct", byName["Point"])
	require.Equal(t, "struct", byName["Tuple"])
	require.Equal(t, "struct", byName["Unit"])
	require.Equal(t, "enum", byName["Color"])
	require.Equal(t, "interface", byName["Greeter"]) // trait -> interface
}

func TestParseItems_ImplMethods(t *testing.T) {

	md, _ := New().Annotate("items.rs", src)

	qualifieds := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {
		qualifieds[f.Qualified] = true
	}
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Point.new"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Point.distance"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Point.hello"]) // from impl Greeter for Point

func TestParseItems_TraitDefaults(t *testing.T) {

		qualifieds[f.Qualified] = true
	}

	// name as receiver so the symbol table can find them.
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Greeter.goodbye"])

func TestParseItems_MacroRules(t *testing.T) {
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Implement items parsing**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/items.go`:
```go
package rust

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseItems extracts fn / struct / enum / trait / impl / macro_rules declarations.
// Returns (functions, classes). impl-block methods are appended to functions
// with Receiver set; trait default-method bodies are also appended with the
// trait name as receiver.
func parseItems(tokens []Token) ([]models.Function, []models.Class) {
	var funcs []models.Function
	var classes []models.Class
	depths := computeBraceDepths(tokens)

	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		if depths[i] > 0 {
			continue
		}
		j := skipItemModifiers(tokens, i)
		if j >= len(tokens) {
			continue
		}
		kw := tokens[j]
		if kw.Kind == TokIdent && kw.Text == "macro_rules" && j+1 < len(tokens) && tokens[j+1].Kind == TokBang {
			if f, end, ok := readMacroRules(tokens, i, j); ok {
				funcs = append(funcs, f)
				i = end
				continue
			}
		}
		if kw.Kind != TokKeyword {
			continue
		}
		switch kw.Text {
		case "fn":
			if f, end, ok := readFn(tokens, i, j, ""); ok {
				funcs = append(funcs, f)
				i = end
			}
		case "struct":
			if c, end, ok := readStruct(tokens, i, j); ok {
				classes = append(classes, c)
				i = end
			}
		case "enum":
			if c, end, ok := readBracedItem(tokens, i, j, "enum"); ok {
				classes = append(classes, c)
				i = end
			}
		case "trait":
			if c, end, ok := readTrait(tokens, i, j); ok {
				classes = append(classes, c)
				// Also collect default method bodies as Functions on the trait.
				methods := readImplOrTraitMethods(tokens, end, c.Name)
				funcs = append(funcs, methods...)
				i = end
			}
		case "impl":
			if recv, bodyClose, ok := readImplHeader(tokens, i, j); ok {
				methods := readImplOrTraitMethods(tokens, bodyClose, recv)
				funcs = append(funcs, methods...)
				i = bodyClose
			}
		}
	}
	return funcs, classes
}

// skipItemModifiers consumes pub / pub(crate) / async / const / unsafe / extern.
func skipItemModifiers(tokens []Token, i int) int {
	j := i
	for j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokKeyword {
		switch tokens[j].Text {
		case "pub":
			j++
			// pub(crate) / pub(super) / pub(in path)
			if j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenParen {
				closeIdx := matchClosingParen(tokens, j)
				if closeIdx >= 0 {
					j = closeIdx + 1
				}
			}
		case "async", "const", "unsafe", "extern", "default":
			j++
		default:
			return j
		}
	}
	return j
}

// matchClosingParen returns the close-paren index that balances openIdx.
func matchClosingParen(tokens []Token, openIdx int) int {
	depth := 0
	for j := openIdx; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenParen {
			depth++
		} else if tokens[j].Kind == TokCloseParen {
			depth--
			if depth == 0 {
				return j
			}
		}
	}
	return -1
}

// readFn reads `fn name<…>(…) -> T { … }`. receiver is empty for free
// functions and the impl/trait type name for methods.
func readFn(tokens []Token, formStart, fnKwIdx int, receiver string) (models.Function, int, bool) {
	nameIdx := fnKwIdx + 1
	if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Function{}, fnKwIdx, false
	}
	name := tokens[nameIdx].Text
	// Find body open brace OR the terminating semicolon (trait method without default).
	bodyStart := -1
	semi := -1
	depthParen, depthAngle := 0, 0
	for k := nameIdx + 1; k < len(tokens); k++ {
		t := tokens[k]
		switch t.Kind {
		case TokOpenParen:
			depthParen++
		case TokCloseParen:
			depthParen--
		case TokOpenAngle:
			depthAngle++
		case TokCloseAngle:
			depthAngle--
		case TokOpenBrace:
			if depthParen == 0 && depthAngle == 0 {
				bodyStart = k
			}
		case TokSemi:
			if depthParen == 0 && depthAngle == 0 && bodyStart < 0 {
				semi = k
			}
		}
		if bodyStart >= 0 || semi >= 0 {
			break
		}
	}
	startLine := tokens[formStart].Line
	endLine := startLine
	end := nameIdx
	if bodyStart >= 0 {
		bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
		if bodyEnd >= 0 {
			endLine = tokens[bodyEnd].Line
			end = bodyEnd
		}
	} else if semi >= 0 {
		// Signature-only fn (trait method without default body) — return false so
		// we don't double-count; trait methods with default bodies go through
		// readImplOrTraitMethods.
		return models.Function{}, semi, false
	} else {
		return models.Function{}, fnKwIdx, false
	}
	qualified := name
	if receiver != "" {
		qualified = receiver + "." + name
	}
	return models.Function{
		Name:      name,
		Receiver:  receiver,
		Qualified: qualified,
		Line:      startLine,
		EndLine:   endLine,
		Signature: renderRustSignature(tokens, formStart, bodyStart),
	}, end, true
}

// readStruct handles three struct shapes:
//   struct Foo;                       — unit struct
//   struct Foo(T, T);                 — tuple struct
//   struct Foo { … }                  — record struct
func readStruct(tokens []Token, formStart, structKwIdx int) (models.Class, int, bool) {
	nameIdx := structKwIdx + 1
	if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Class{}, structKwIdx, false
	}
	name := tokens[nameIdx].Text
	// Skip generic parameters <…>.
	after := nameIdx + 1
	if after < len(tokens) && tokens[after].Kind == TokOpenAngle {
		closeIdx := matchAngleClose(tokens, after)
		if closeIdx >= 0 {
			after = closeIdx + 1
		}
	}
	// Three end shapes: `;` (unit), `(…);` (tuple), `{ … }` (record).
	if after >= len(tokens) {
		return models.Class{}, structKwIdx, false
	}
	startLine := tokens[formStart].Line
	endLine := startLine
	end := after
	switch tokens[after].Kind {
	case TokSemi:
		end = after
		endLine = tokens[after].Line
	case TokOpenParen:
		closeIdx := matchClosingParen(tokens, after)
		if closeIdx >= 0 {
			end = closeIdx
			endLine = tokens[closeIdx].Line
		}
		// Possibly a trailing `;`.
		if end+1 < len(tokens) && tokens[end+1].Kind == TokSemi {
			end++
			endLine = tokens[end].Line
		}
	case TokOpenBrace:
		closeIdx := matchClosingBrace(tokens, after)
		if closeIdx >= 0 {
			end = closeIdx
			endLine = tokens[closeIdx].Line
		}
	default:
		return models.Class{}, structKwIdx, false
	}
	return models.Class{
		Name:      name,
		Qualified: name,
		Kind:      "struct",
		Line:      startLine,
		EndLine:   endLine,
	}, end, true
}

// readBracedItem reads `enum Name<…> { … }` shape (works for enum; not used
// for struct because struct has multiple non-brace shapes).
func readBracedItem(tokens []Token, formStart, kwIdx int, kind string) (models.Class, int, bool) {
	nameIdx := kwIdx + 1
	if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Class{}, kwIdx, false
	}
	name := tokens[nameIdx].Text
	bodyStart := findNextOpenBraceRust(tokens, nameIdx+1)
	if bodyStart < 0 {
		return models.Class{}, kwIdx, false
	}
	bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
	if bodyEnd < 0 {
		return models.Class{}, kwIdx, false
	}
	return models.Class{
		Name:      name,
		Qualified: name,
		Kind:      kind,
		Line:      tokens[formStart].Line,
		EndLine:   tokens[bodyEnd].Line,
	}, bodyEnd, true
}

// readTrait reads `trait Name<…> [: Supertrait] { … }`. Maps to Class.Kind = "interface".
func readTrait(tokens []Token, formStart, kwIdx int) (models.Class, int, bool) {
	c, end, ok := readBracedItem(tokens, formStart, kwIdx, "interface")
	return c, end, ok
}

// readImplHeader reads `impl<…> Type` or `impl<…> Trait for Type`.
// Returns the receiver type name (the Type after `for`, or the bare type
// after `impl …<…>`), the body-close index, and whether the read succeeded.
func readImplHeader(tokens []Token, formStart, implKwIdx int) (string, int, bool) {
	// Skip optional generic params <…> immediately after `impl`.
	j := implKwIdx + 1
	if j < len(tokens) && tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenAngle {
		closeIdx := matchAngleClose(tokens, j)
		if closeIdx >= 0 {
			j = closeIdx + 1
		}
	}
	// Walk forward, collecting identifier-style path components for the
	// "lhs" type, until we hit either `for` or `{`.
	var lhs []string
	var rhs []string
	target := &lhs
	for k := j; k < len(tokens); k++ {
		t := tokens[k]
		if t.Kind == TokKeyword && t.Text == "for" {
			target = &rhs
			continue
		}
		if t.Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			bodyClose := matchClosingBrace(tokens, k)
			if bodyClose < 0 {
				return "", k, false
			}
			recv := lastIdent(lhs)
			if len(rhs) > 0 {
				recv = lastIdent(rhs)
			}
			if recv == "" {
				return "", bodyClose, false
			}
			return recv, bodyClose, true
		}
		// Skip generic / lifetime baggage; collect bare idents for the type.
		if t.Kind == TokIdent {
			*target = append(*target, t.Text)
		}
	}
	return "", implKwIdx, false
}

// lastIdent returns the last element of idents (e.g. for ["std","collections","HashMap"]
// returns "HashMap"), or "" when empty.
func lastIdent(idents []string) string {
	if len(idents) == 0 {
		return ""
	}
	return idents[len(idents)-1]
}

// readImplOrTraitMethods scans an impl/trait body for `fn name…` items and
// returns them as Methods with Receiver = ownerName. The body is the brace
// block that ends at bodyCloseIdx; we walk backwards from that to find the
// matching open brace.
func readImplOrTraitMethods(tokens []Token, bodyCloseIdx int, ownerName string) []models.Function {
	if bodyCloseIdx <= 0 || bodyCloseIdx >= len(tokens) {
		return nil
	}
	// Find matching open brace by walking backwards.
	openIdx := -1
	depth := 1
	for k := bodyCloseIdx - 1; k >= 0; k-- {
		if tokens[k].Kind == TokCloseBrace {
			depth++
		} else if tokens[k].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			depth--
			if depth == 0 {
				openIdx = k
				break
			}
		}
	}
	if openIdx < 0 {
		return nil
	}
	bodyDepth := computeBraceDepths(tokens)[openIdx] + 1
	depths := computeBraceDepths(tokens)
	var out []models.Function
	for i := openIdx + 1; i < bodyCloseIdx; i++ {
		if depths[i] != bodyDepth {
			continue
		}
		j := skipItemModifiers(tokens, i)
		if j >= len(tokens) || tokens[j].Kind != TokKeyword || tokens[j].Text != "fn" {
			continue
		}
		if f, end, ok := readFn(tokens, i, j, ownerName); ok {
			out = append(out, f)
			i = end
		}
	}
	return out
}

// readMacroRules reads `macro_rules! name { … }`.
func readMacroRules(tokens []Token, formStart, identIdx int) (models.Function, int, bool) {
	// identIdx is `macro_rules`; identIdx+1 is `!`.
	nameIdx := identIdx + 2
	if nameIdx >= len(tokens) || tokens[nameIdx].Kind != TokIdent {
		return models.Function{}, identIdx, false
	}
	name := tokens[nameIdx].Text
	bodyStart := findNextOpenBraceRust(tokens, nameIdx+1)
	if bodyStart < 0 {
		return models.Function{}, identIdx, false
	}
	bodyEnd := matchClosingBrace(tokens, bodyStart)
	if bodyEnd < 0 {
		return models.Function{}, identIdx, false
	}
	return models.Function{
		Name:      name,
		Qualified: name,
		Line:      tokens[formStart].Line,
		EndLine:   tokens[bodyEnd].Line,
		Signature: "macro_rules! " + name,
	}, bodyEnd, true
}

// matchAngleClose returns the close-angle index that balances openIdx.
// Rust generics may nest (`Vec<HashMap<K, V>>`); we count `<` / `>` depth.
// Edge case: `>>` can be ambiguous (could be two `>`s or a right-shift); we
// don't handle that — the scanner emits two TokCloseAngle tokens so it works
// in practice.
func matchAngleClose(tokens []Token, openIdx int) int {
	depth := 0
	for j := openIdx; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenAngle {
			depth++
		} else if tokens[j].Kind == TokCloseAngle {
			depth--
			if depth == 0 {
				return j
			}
		}
	}
	return -1
}

// findNextOpenBraceRust returns the index of the next TokOpenBrace at or after i.
func findNextOpenBraceRust(tokens []Token, i int) int {
	for j := i; j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if tokens[j].Kind == TokOpenBrace {
			return j
		}
	}
	return -1
}

// renderRustSignature joins token text between start and signatureEnd into
// a single-line signature.
func renderRustSignature(tokens []Token, start, signatureEnd int) string {
	if signatureEnd <= start {
		return ""
	}
	var b []byte
	for j := start; j < signatureEnd && j < len(tokens); j++ {
		if len(b) > 0 {
			b = append(b, ' ')
		}
		b = append(b, []byte(tokens[j].Text)...)
	}
	return string(b)
}
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Wire items into Annotate**

```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "rust",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}
	tokens := Scan(source)
	md.Imports = parseUses(tokens)
	modImps, modClasses := parseMods(tokens)
	md.Imports = append(md.Imports, modImps...)
	md.Classes = append(md.Classes, modClasses...)
	itemFuncs, itemClasses := parseItems(tokens)
	md.Functions = append(md.Functions, itemFuncs...)
	md.Classes = append(md.Classes, itemClasses...)
	return md, nil
}
```

```bash
Free fns + methods (impl + trait defaults), unit/tuple/record structs,
enums (variants kept opaque), traits (Kind=interface in models.Class),
macro_rules (name-only, body opaque). Modifier set: pub/pub(crate)/
async/const/unsafe/extern/default. impl-header parser handles both
'impl Type' and 'impl Trait for Type' — Receiver always = implementing
type, never the trait."
```

## Task 17: Call edges (Rust)

**Files:**
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/calls.go`
- Create: `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/calls.rs.txt`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/rust/annotator.go`
- Modify: `internal/annotator/rust/annotator_test.go`

Rust call edges, like TS:

- `helper()` → `To = "helper"`
- `pkg::fn()` → `To = "pkg::fn"` (we keep the `::` separator)
- `obj.method()` → `To = "obj.method"`
- `self.method()` → `To = "self.method"` (graph resolver normalises later)
- `Foo::bar()` → `To = "Foo::bar"` (associated function call)

Macro calls (`println!`, `format!`, `vec!`) get one edge per invocation with `To = "name!"` (trailing `!` to mark it as a macro).

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/calls.rs.txt`:
```
fn helper(x: i32) -> i32 { x + 1 }

fn outer() -> i32 {
    let a = helper(1);
    let b = helper(2);
    println!("a={}, b={}", a, b);
    std::cmp::max(a, b)
}

struct Counter { n: i32 }

impl Counter {
    fn new() -> Self { Counter { n: 0 } }
    fn tick(&mut self) { self.n += 1; }
    fn run(&mut self) -> i32 {
        self.tick();
        self.tick();
        Self::report(self.n)
    }
    fn report(n: i32) -> i32 { n }
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the failing test**

Append to `annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestParseCalls_FreeFn(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "calls.rs.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("calls.rs", src)
	tos := callTos(md.Calls, "outer")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "helper")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "std::cmp::max")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "println!")
}

func TestParseCalls_MethodAndAssoc(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "calls.rs.txt")
	md, _ := New().Annotate("calls.rs", src)
	tos := callTos(md.Calls, "Counter.run")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "self.tick")
	require.Contains(t, tos, "Self::report")
}

func callTos(edges []models.SymbolRef, from string) []string {
	var out []string
	for _, e := range edges {
		if e.From == from {
			out = append(out, e.To)
		}
	}
	return out
}
```

- [ ] **Step 3: Implement the call extractor**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/calls.go`:
```go
package rust

import (
	"strings"

	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

// parseCalls walks the token stream and emits one SymbolRef per call site
// inside any of the supplied functions.
//
// To-field shapes:
//   helper()         -> To = "helper"
//   pkg::fn()        -> To = "pkg::fn"
//   Foo::new()       -> To = "Foo::new"
//   self.method()    -> To = "self.method"
//   obj.method()     -> To = "obj.method"
//   println!()       -> To = "println!"
//
// Method/assoc calls on non-identifier receivers (e.g. `(a + b).foo()`) are
// skipped.
func parseCalls(tokens []Token, funcs []models.Function) []models.SymbolRef {
	if len(tokens) == 0 || len(funcs) == 0 {
		return nil
	}
	var out []models.SymbolRef

	for i := 0; i < len(tokens); i++ {
		t := tokens[i]
		var target string
		end := i

		// Macro call: ident !
		if t.Kind == TokIdent && i+1 < len(tokens) && tokens[i+1].Kind == TokBang {
			target = t.Text + "!"
			end = i + 1
			// Macro body can use (), [], or {}; we just need to detect the call.
			callLine := t.Line
			from := enclosingFunction(funcs, callLine)
			if from != "" {
				out = append(out, models.SymbolRef{From: from, To: target, Line: callLine})
			}
			i = end
			continue
		}

		// Build qualified target by walking idents joined by `::` or `.`.
		if t.Kind != TokIdent && !(t.Kind == TokKeyword && (t.Text == "self" || t.Text == "Self")) {
			continue
		}
		path := []string{t.Text}
		seps := []string{}
		end = i
		for {
			if end+2 >= len(tokens) {
				break
			}
			sep := tokens[end+1]
			nxt := tokens[end+2]
			if sep.Kind == TokDoubleColon && nxt.Kind == TokIdent {
				path = append(path, nxt.Text)
				seps = append(seps, "::")
				end += 2
				continue
			}
			if sep.Kind == TokPunct && sep.Text == "." && nxt.Kind == TokIdent {
				path = append(path, nxt.Text)
				seps = append(seps, ".")
				end += 2
				continue
			}
			break
		}
		// After path, must be `(`.
		if end+1 >= len(tokens) || tokens[end+1].Kind != TokOpenParen {
			continue
		}
		// Reconstruct the target with original separators.
		target = path[0]
		for k := 0; k < len(seps); k++ {
			target += seps[k] + path[k+1]
		}

		callLine := t.Line
		from := enclosingFunction(funcs, callLine)
		if from == "" {
			continue
		}
		out = append(out, models.SymbolRef{From: from, To: target, Line: callLine})
		i = end
	}
	return out
}

// enclosingFunction picks the innermost function whose range covers line.
func enclosingFunction(funcs []models.Function, line int) string {
	best := ""
	bestRange := 1 << 30
	for _, f := range funcs {
		if line < f.Line || line > f.EndLine {
			continue
		}
		r := f.EndLine - f.Line
		if r < bestRange {
			bestRange = r
			best = f.Qualified
		}
	}
	return best
}

// (unused — kept for symmetry with TS package)
var _ = strings.Join
```

- [ ] **Step 4: Wire calls into Annotate**

```go
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "rust",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}
	tokens := Scan(source)
	md.Imports = parseUses(tokens)
	modImps, modClasses := parseMods(tokens)
	md.Imports = append(md.Imports, modImps...)
	md.Classes = append(md.Classes, modClasses...)
	itemFuncs, itemClasses := parseItems(tokens)
	md.Functions = append(md.Functions, itemFuncs...)
	md.Classes = append(md.Classes, itemClasses...)
	md.Calls = parseCalls(tokens, md.Functions)
	return md, nil
}
```

```bash
Targets preserve the source separator: '::' for paths/assocs ('Foo::new',
'std::cmp::max'), '.' for methods ('self.tick'). Macros end with '!'
('println!'). Non-identifier callees skipped (matches Go/TS posture)."
```

## Task 18: Rust end-to-end test + binary wiring

**Files:**

- [ ] **Step 1: Create the realistic fixture**

Create `internal/annotator/rust/testdata/realistic.rs.txt` (modelled on a `ripgrep`-style search module):
```
//! Realistic Rust fixture: a tiny search module.

use std::collections::HashMap;
use std::io::{self, BufRead, BufReader, Read};
use std::path::PathBuf;

mod regex_engine;
mod settings;

pub use crate::error::SearchError;

#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
pub struct SearchHit {
    pub path: PathBuf,
    pub line: usize,
    pub text: String,
}

#[derive(Debug)]
pub struct Searcher<'a> {
    pattern: &'a str,
    case_insensitive: bool,
    hits: Vec<SearchHit>,
}

pub trait Source {
    fn read(&self) -> io::Result<String>;
    fn label(&self) -> &str {
        "unknown"
    }
}

impl<'a> Searcher<'a> {
    pub fn new(pattern: &'a str) -> Self {
        Searcher { pattern, case_insensitive: false, hits: Vec::new() }
    }

    pub fn case_insensitive(mut self, on: bool) -> Self {
        self.case_insensitive = on;
        self
    }

    pub fn search<R: Read>(&mut self, reader: R, path: PathBuf) -> Result<usize, SearchError> {
        let buf = BufReader::new(reader);
        let mut total = 0usize;
        for (n, line) in buf.lines().enumerate() {
            let line = line?;
            if self.matches(&line) {
                self.hits.push(SearchHit { path: path.clone(), line: n + 1, text: line });
                total += 1;
            }
        }
        Ok(total)
    }

    fn matches(&self, line: &str) -> bool {
        if self.case_insensitive {
            line.to_lowercase().contains(&self.pattern.to_lowercase())
        } else {
            line.contains(self.pattern)
        }
    }

    pub fn hits(&self) -> &[SearchHit] {
        &self.hits
    }
}

impl<'a> Source for Searcher<'a> {
    fn read(&self) -> io::Result<String> {
        Ok(format!("searcher({})", self.pattern))
    }
}

pub enum Match {
    None,
    Found(usize),
    Many(Vec<usize>),
}

macro_rules! count_hits {
    ($s:expr) => { $s.hits().len() };
}
```

- [ ] **Step 2: Write the end-to-end test**

Append to `annotator_test.go`:
```go
func TestAnnotate_RealisticRust_E2E(t *testing.T) {
	src := mustReadFixture(t, "realistic.rs.txt")
	md, err := New().Annotate("realistic.rs", src)
	require.NoError(t, err)

	// Imports.
	paths := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, im := range md.Imports {
		paths[im.Path] = true
	}
	require.True(t, paths["std::collections::HashMap"])
	require.True(t, paths["std::path::PathBuf"])
	require.True(t, paths["regex_engine"]) // file mod
	require.True(t, paths["settings"])

	// Types.
	kinds := make(map[string]string)
	for _, c := range md.Classes {
		kinds[c.Name] = c.Kind
	}
	require.Equal(t, "struct", kinds["SearchHit"])
	require.Equal(t, "struct", kinds["Searcher"])
	require.Equal(t, "interface", kinds["Source"]) // trait
	require.Equal(t, "enum", kinds["Match"])

	// Methods.
	qualifieds := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {
		qualifieds[f.Qualified] = true
	}
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Searcher.new"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Searcher.case_insensitive"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Searcher.search"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Searcher.matches"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Searcher.hits"])
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Searcher.read"]) // impl Source for Searcher
	require.True(t, qualifieds["Source.label"])  // trait default

	// Macro.
	macros := make(map[string]bool)
	for _, f := range md.Functions {
		macros[f.Name] = true
	}
	require.True(t, macros["count_hits"])
}
```

## Phase 4: Java annotator

Java is structurally close to TypeScript (block-scoped, brace-delimited declarations), so the patterns from Phase 2 transfer. Java-specific complications:

- **Annotations:** `@Override`, `@RestController`, `@RequestMapping("/path")`. We collect annotation names onto the next-declared class/method (recorded as a flat `[]string` field via abuse of `Signature` for M2 — full annotation-shape support is M3+).
- **Generics ambiguity:** Java has `<>` generics but **no JSX**, so the disambiguation is easier than TS. We don't need a context heuristic; we just track angle-bracket depth like Rust.
- **Records:** `record Point(int x, int y) {}` lands in Java 14+. Treat as Class with `Kind = "class"` (we don't model "record" separately in `models.Class` for M2).
- **Nested classes:** Inner class declarations should be detected and their methods attributed to `Outer.Inner.method`. We accept lossier nesting for M2 — top-level + one level deep is enough for the fidelity gate on `spring-petclinic`.

Python annotator: `src/token_savior/java_annotator.py` (~1228 LoC, the largest in Python's tree). Grep `_CLASS_RE`, `_METHOD_RE`, `_PACKAGE_RE`, `_IMPORT_RE`, `_ANNOTATION_RE` for shape reference.


- [ ] **Step 4: Create the skeleton**

Create `internal/annotator/java/annotator.go`:
```go
// Package java annotates Java source (.java) using a hand-rolled tokenizer.
// Scope: package, import, class/interface/enum/record declarations, methods,
// and annotation names (collected onto the following declaration).
//
// Lossier than tree-sitter on deeply-nested generics and lambdas — see
// spec §173. Accepted for M2; fidelity-script measures real-world coverage.
package java

import (
	"token-savior-go/internal/annotator"
	"token-savior-go/internal/models"
)

func init() {
	annotator.Register("java", New())
}

// Annotator is the Java annotator. Safe for concurrent use.
type Annotator struct{}

// New returns a Java annotator.
func New() *Annotator { return &Annotator{} }

// Annotate parses Java source and emits structural metadata.
func (a *Annotator) Annotate(path string, source []byte) (*models.StructuralMetadata, error) {
	md := &models.StructuralMetadata{
		Path:       path,
		Language:   "java",
		Functions:  []models.Function{},
		Classes:    []models.Class{},
		Imports:    []models.Import{},
		Calls:      []models.SymbolRef{},
		References: []models.SymbolRef{},
	}
	if len(source) == 0 {
		return md, nil
	}
	// Task 20-23 fill in.
	return md, nil
}
```

- [ ] **Step 5: Run the tests**

Run:
```bash
go test ./internal/annotator/java/ -v
```
Expected: PASS for all three.

- [ ] **Step 6: Commit**

```bash
git add internal/annotator/java/
git commit -m "feat(annotator/java): skeleton + dispatch for .java

Zero-result Annotate so the indexer can dispatch. Scanner + item
parsers land in T20-T23."
```
